فقال لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( هم قومك يا أبا موسى أهل اليمن ).
The Ash'aris, among them Abu Musa, began to recite poetry saying, 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.' This was narrated by Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Nasa'i in his Sunan from Ibn Muthanna from Ibn al-Harith from Humaid. Al-Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Faqih informed us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Mansur ibn Khalaf al-Bazzaz reported to us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abdullah Muhammad al-Shaybani al-Jawzaqi reported to us: Abu Hamid ibn al-Sharqi reported to us: Muhammad ibn Hayawayh reported to us: Abu al-Yaman reported to us: Shu'ayb reported to us, saying: Abu al-Zinad reported to us from al-A'raj from Abu Hurairah from him, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the weakest in hearts and the most tender in feelings. Faith is Yemenite, and wisdom is Yemenite. The head of unbelief is towards the east, and pride and arrogance are among the owners of camels and horses—the owners of camels are the people of wool—and tranquility is among the owners of sheep.' Al-Shaykh Abu Abdullah al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Malik al-Khallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Ibrahim ibn Mansur ibn Ibrahim al-Sulami reported to us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn al-Muqri' reported to us: Abu Ya'la Ahmad ibn Ali ibn al-Muthanna al-Mawsili reported to us: Abu Khaythamah reported to us: Jarir reported to us from al-A'mash from Abu Salih from Abu Hurairah, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Faith is Yemenite, and wisdom is Yemenite. The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the most tender in feelings and the softest in hearts.' It was recorded by al-Bukhari and Muslim in their Sahihs; Muslim narrated it from Abu Khaythamah. Abu Bakr Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirawi informed us of it in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad al-Tabasi in Nishapur narrated to me from him, saying: The judge Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ahmad al-Hayri reported to us—and we were also informed of it by Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn reported to us: Abu Abdullah al-Hafiz reported to us, both saying: Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub reported to us: Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar reported to us: Abu Mu'awiyah reported to us from al-A'mash from Abu Salih from Abu Hurairah, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the softest in hearts and the most tender in feelings. Faith is Yemenite, and wisdom is Yemenite.' Al-Hayri added: Abu Mu'awiyah said: I think he said: 'The head of unbelief is towards the east.' Al-Shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Muqri' in Baghdad informed us: The noble judge Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Ubayd Allah ibn Abd al-Samad ibn al-Muhtadi Billah reported to us: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Umar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Shadhan al-Sukri al-Harbi reported to us, saying: Abu Habib al-Abbas ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Isa reported to us: Isma'il ibn bint al-Busri reported to us: Husayn ibn Isa reported to us from Ma'mar from al-Zuhri from Abu Hazim from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, who said: While the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was in Medina, he said: 'Allahu Akbar! The help of Allah and the conquest have come, and the people of Yemen have come.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what are the people of Yemen? He said: 'A people with tender hearts, obedient, faith is Yemenite, jurisprudence is Yemenite, and wisdom is Yemenite.' Abu Mas'ud Abd al-Rahim ibn Ali ibn Hamd informed us: Abu Ali al-Haddad reported to us: Abu Nu'aym al-Hafiz reported to us: Sulayman ibn Ahmad reported to us: Ahmad ibn Amr al-Qatrani reported to us: Sulayman ibn Harb reported to us—and Abu Nu'aym also reported to us, saying: al-Ghitrifi reported to us: Abu Khalifah reported to us: al-Hawdi reported to us, both saying: Shu'bah reported to us from Simak ibn Harb from Iyad al-Ash'ari that when 'Soon will Allah bring a people whom He loves and who love Him' was revealed, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'They are this people,' and he struck his hand on the back of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Abu Nu'aym said: Idris al-Awdi narrated it from Simak. Al-Shaykh Abu Muhammad Abd al-Karim ibn Hamzah ibn al-Khidr al-Sulami in Damascus informed us: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz reported to us: Abu al-Qasim Tammam ibn Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Razi reported to us: my father, may Allah have mercy on him, reported to us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad Abd al-Aziz ibn al-Ja'd al-Washsha' in Baghdad reported to us: Abu Ma'mar Isma'il ibn Ibrahim al-Quti'i reported to us: Abdullah ibn Idris reported to us from his father from Simak ibn Harb from Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, who said: (The verse) 'Soon will Allah bring a people whom He loves and who love Him' was recited before the Prophet, peace be upon him. He said: 'They are your people, O Abu Musa, the people of Yemen.' Al-Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Faqih informed us: Abu Bakr al-Khusrujirdi reported to us: Abu Tahir al-Faqih reported to us: Abu Abdullah al-Saffar reported to us: Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal reported to us: Abu Ma'mar narrated to me: Abdullah ibn Idris reported to us from his father from Ibn Harb from Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa, who said: (The verse) 'Soon will Allah bring a people whom He loves and who love Him' was recited before the Prophet, peace be upon him. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to me: 'They are your people, O Abu Musa, the people of Yemen.'
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of multiple hadith narrations all centered on praising the people of Yemen, particularly the Ash'aris. The author, Ibn Asakir, is gathering these traditions as proofs to support the virtue of the Ash'ari school, since the founder Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari was from Yemen. The first hadith describes the Ash'aris reciting poetry and then reports a famous hadith from Abu Hurairah about the Yemenites having weak hearts (i.e., soft and humble) and being characterized by faith and wisdom. The second narration emphasizes that faith and wisdom are Yemenite, and the people of Yemen possess tender feelings. The third adds that the head of unbelief is towards the east. The fourth from Ibn Abbas mentions that the Prophet declared the arrival of the people of Yemen as a conquest and described them as having tender hearts and obedience. The later narrations focus on the verse 'Soon will Allah bring a people whom He loves and who love Him' (5:54), which the Prophet interpreted as referring to the Ash'aris, specifically pointing to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Each hadith is presented with its full chain of transmission to demonstrate authenticity. The cumulative effect is to show that the Ash'aris are a blessed group beloved by Allah, thus defending the school against detractors.

Key Terms
الأشعريون
أبو موسى الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the verse refers to any group of believers, but the hadith specifies the Ash'aris.
Correction: The Prophet's explicit gesture and words indicate that the Ash'aris are the intended people.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, when the verse 'Soon will Allah bring a people whom He loves and who love Him' was revealed, who did the Prophet identify as that people?
A) The Quraysh
B) The Ansar
C) The Ash'aris, indicated by pointing to Abu Musa
D) The Muhajirun

Key Takeaway
The Prophet identified the Ash'aris as the beloved people of Allah through a direct gesture to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet specifically identified a group as beloved by Allah. If you consider yourself part of the Ash'ari school, does this fill you with confidence or complacency? Do you live as if you are among those who truly love Allah, or do you rely on affiliation alone? What concrete steps can you take today to deepen your love for Allah and earn His love?
?
When you read the verse 'a people whom He loves and who love Him,' do you feel that description applies to you personally? If not, what is missing in your relationship with Allah that prevents that mutual love? Are you willing to examine your priorities and change what is necessary to become one of those people?
?
The Prophet's gesture was public and deliberate. Imagine you were present; would you have understood the weight of that sign? Today, knowing that the Ash'aris were honored, how does that challenge you to live up to the qualities of that group? What is one attribute of the Ash'aris (like their commitment to Ahl al-Sunna) that you need to cultivate more urgently in your own life?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
4 min
The Prophet's Praise of the Yemeni People
Hadith praising the people of Yemen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic praise of the people of Yemen and their special qualities of faith, jurisprudence, and wisdom.

Core Idea
The Prophet declared faith, fiqh, and wisdom to be Yemeni.

This lesson presents a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas in which the Prophet, while in Medina, praises the people of Yemen. The description highlights their tender hearts and soft obedience, and attributes the very essence of faith, Islamic jurisprudence, and wisdom to Yemen. This sets the stage for the honored status of the Ash'ari school, rooted in Yemeni origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic and translation of the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas. Notice the context: the Prophet announces the coming of the people of Yemen.
2
Identify the three attributes
The Prophet describes the Yemeni people with three core qualities: faith, jurisprudence (fiqh), and wisdom (hikma). Note that these are attributed as 'Yemeni'.
This indicates the spiritual excellence of Yemen.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the Prophet would specifically praise Yemen in this way. This hadith becomes a foundation for the Ash'ari claim to virtue, as Imam al-Ash'ari was of Yemeni descent.
The Ash'ari school traces its origin to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, a Yemeni companion.

أبي الحسن الأشعري رضي الله عنه، فهو من قوم أبي موسى وأولاده الذين أوتوا العلم ورزقوا الفهم، مخصوصا من بينهم بتقوية السنة وقمع البدعة بإظهار الحجة ورد الشبهة. والأشبه أن يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه بمشيئة الله وإذنه. أعاننا الله تعالى على ذلك بمنه وختم بالسعادة والشهادة بجوده. وليعلم المنصف من أصحابنا صنع الله تعالى في تقديم هذا الأصل الشريف لما ذخر لعباده من هذا الفرع المنيف الذي أحيا به السنة وأمات به البدعة، وجعله خلف حق لسلف صدق. أخبرنا أبو الفتح محمد بن علي بن عبد الله المصري وأبو بكر ناصر بن أبي العباس بن علي الصيدلاني بهراة قالا أنبا محمد بن عبد العزيز الفارسي أنبا عبد الرحمن بن أحمد ونسبا. أخبرنا الشيخان أبو القاسم عبد الملك بن عبد الله بن داود المغربي وأبو غالب محمد بن الحسن بن علي البصري الماوردي ببغداد قالا أنبا أبو علي علي بن أحمد بن علي التستري بالبصرة ثنا القاضي الشريف أبو Al-Hamd ibn 'Isa narrated to us: Isma'il ibn bint al-Bisri narrated to us: Husayn ibn 'Isa narrated to us from Ma'mar from al-Zuhri from Abu Hazim from Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, who said: While the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was in Medina, he said: 'Allahu akbar, the help of Allah and the conquest have come, and the people of Yemen have come.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what are the people of Yemen? He said: 'A people with tender hearts, soft in obedience, faith is Yemeni, jurisprudence is Yemeni, wisdom is Yemeni.' Abu Mas'ud 'Abd al-Rahim ibn 'Ali ibn Hamd informed us: Abu 'Ali al-Haddad reported to us: Abu Nu'aym al-Hafiz reported to us: Sulayman ibn Ahmad narrated to us: Ahmad ibn 'Amr al-Qatrani narrated to us: Sulayman ibn Jarb (h). And Abu Nu'aym informed us, saying: al-Ghatrifi narrated to us: Abu Khalifa narrated to us: al-Hawdi narrated to us: they said: Shu'ba narrated to us from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari: When {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} was revealed, the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'They are the people of this one' and struck his hand on the back of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Abu Nu'aym said: Idris al-Awdi narrated it from Simak. The Shaykh Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-Karim ibn Hamza ibn al-Khadir al-Sulami in Damascus informed us: Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz narrated to us: Abu al-Qasim Tamam ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Razi reported to us: my father, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated to us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn al-Ja'd al-Washa' in Baghdad narrated to us: Abu Mu'mar Isma'il ibn Ibrahim al-Qati'i narrated to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from his father from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari who said: It was recited before the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} and he said: 'They are your people, the people of Yemen.' The Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Faqih informed us: Abu Bakr al-Khasrujirdi reported to us: Abu Tahir al-Faqih reported to us: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Saffar reported to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated to us: Abu Mu'mar narrated to me: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from his father from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa who said: It was recited before the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} and the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said to me: 'They are your people, O Abu Musa, the people of Yemen.' The Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi informed us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi al-Hafiz reported to us, saying: To proceed: Some of the Ash'ari imams mentioned to me the text of the hadith which Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us: Abu al-'Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub narrated to us: Ibrahim ibn Marzuq narrated to us: Wahb ibn Jarir and Abu 'Amir al-'Aqadi narrated to us: they said: Shu'ba narrated to us from Simak. And Abu Bakr 'Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirawi informed us in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin 'Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr al-Tabasi in Nishapur narrated to me from him, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Hayri reported to us: Muhammad ibn Ya'qub narrated to us: Ibrahim ibn Marzuq narrated to us: Wahb from Shu'ba narrated to us, and he said: Ibrahim narrated to us: Abu 'Amir from Shu'ba from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari who said: When {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} was revealed, the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, gestured towards Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with him, and said: 'They are the people of this one.' Al-Bayhaqi said: That is because of the great virtue and noble rank found in him for Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, for he is from the people of Abu Musa and his descendants who were given knowledge and granted understanding, distinguished among them by strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation by manifesting proof and refuting doubts. It is more likely that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, only made the people of Abu Musa among the people Allah loves and who love Him because of what he knew of the soundness of their religion and what he recognized of the strength of their certainty. So whoever follows their way in the science of principles (usul) and follows their statement in negating anthropomorphism while adhering to the Book and Sunnah, he is made among their number and counted among their company by the will and permission of Allah. May Allah Almighty help us to that by His grace and seal with happiness and martyrdom by His bounty. And let the fair-minded among our companions know the act of Allah Almighty in presenting this noble origin for what He has stored for His servants of this lofty branch, by which He revived the Sunnah and killed innovation, and made it a true successor to a truthful predecessor. Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn 'Abd Allah al-Misri and Abu Bakr Nasir ibn Abi al-'Abbas ibn 'Ali al-Saydalani in Herat informed us: they said: Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Farisi reported to us: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Shurayh reported to us: Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id narrated to us: Abu Sa'id al-Ashajj narrated to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from Layth from Mujahid regarding His word, exalted: {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} he said: The people of Saba', and the Ash'aris are a people from Saba'. How noble is that origin and lineage! The two shaykhs Abu al-Qasim 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Dawud al-Maghribi and Abu Ghalib Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Basri al-Mawardi in Baghdad informed us: they said: Abu 'Ali 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Tustari in Basra reported to us: the judge al-Sharif Abu 'Umar
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a multi-chain hadith report and scholarly commentary establishing the virtue of the Ash'ari school. It begins with a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas describing the people of Yemen as having tender hearts and being the source of faith, jurisprudence, and wisdom. Then multiple chains from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari report that when the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him' was revealed, the Prophet pointed to Abu Musa and said 'They are the people of this one' or explicitly said 'They are your people, the people of Yemen.' This identifies the 'people Allah loves' as the Ash'aris (descendants of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari). The author then quotes al-Bayhaqi's commentary, which explains that this hadith indicates the great virtue of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who is from the people of Abu Musa, and that the Prophet's statement applies to all who follow the Ash'ari methodology in usul al-din (principles of religion) by negating anthropomorphism (tashbih) while adhering to the Quran and Sunnah. The passage concludes with a chain from Mujahid that the promised people are from Saba', and the Ash'aris are from Saba', thus further ennobling their origin. The overall argument is that the Ash'ari school is rooted in prophetic praise and therefore legitimate and praiseworthy.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, which of the following did the Prophet specifically attribute to Yemen?
A) Wealth and trade
B) Faith, jurisprudence, and wisdom
C) Military strength
D) Poetry and eloquence

Key Takeaway
The Prophet praised the people of Yemen, making faith, fiqh, and wisdom Yemeni characteristics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet described the Yemeni people as having tender hearts and soft obedience. Look at your own heart: are you tender towards the truth and soft in submitting to Allah's commands? What is one area today where you can practice soft obedience?
?
Faith, fiqh, and wisdom are said to be Yemeni qualities. Which of these three do you feel is weakest in your own life, and what concrete step will you take this week to strengthen it based on what you have learned?
?
This hadith shows that Allah blessed a particular people with special virtues. Do you ever feel envious of such blessings? Instead, ask yourself: Are you striving to acquire these same virtues regardless of your lineage? What will you change starting today?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
5 min
Prophetic Identification of the Beloved People
Multiple hadith chains identifying the people Allah loves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet identified the people mentioned in Quran 5:54 as Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and his people, the Ash'aris of Yemen.

Core Idea
The Prophet pointed to Abu Musa and said, 'They are the people of this one.'

This lesson presents multiple hadith chains that report the Prophet's reaction to the revelation of the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him.' In each report, the Prophet explicitly points to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari or states that the people are the Yemeni Ash'aris. These reports form the core evidence for the Ash'ari school's honored status.

Guided Path
1
Read the multiple hadith chains
Read the Arabic and translation of the collection of hadith reports. Notice that each chain ends with the same core message: the Prophet identifies the people as Abu Musa's people or the Yemeni people.
The multiple chains strengthen the reliability of the report.
2
Identify the different phrasings
Note the variations: in one chain the Prophet strikes Abu Musa's back and says 'They are the people of this one'; in another he says 'They are your people, the people of Yemen'; in a third he gestures and says the same.
All variations point to the same identification.
3
Understand the significance
The verse is thus interpreted as referring to the Ash'aris (the tribe of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari). This direct prophetic identification is a key proof for the virtue of the Ash'ari school.
This counters the misconception that the verse refers to a future unrelated group.

أبي الحسن الأشعري رضي الله عنه، فهو من قوم أبي موسى وأولاده الذين أوتوا العلم ورزقوا الفهم، مخصوصا من بينهم بتقوية السنة وقمع البدعة بإظهار الحجة ورد الشبهة. والأشبه أن يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إنما جعل قوم أبي موسى من قوم يحبهم الله ويحبونه، لما علم من صحة دينهم وعرف من قوة يقينهم، فمن نحا في علم الأصول نحوهم وتبع في نفي التشبيه مع ملازمة الكتاب والسنة قولهم جعل من جملتهم وعد من حسابهم بمشيئة الله وإذنه. أعاننا الله تعالى على ذلك بمنه وختم بالسعادة والشهادة بجوده. وليعلم المنصف من أصحابنا صنع الله تعالى في تقديم هذا الأصل الشريف لما ذخر لعباده من هذا الفرع المنيف الذي أحيا به السنة وأمات به البدعة، وجعله خلف حق لسلف صدق. أخبرنا أبو الفتح محمد بن علي بن عبد الله المصري وأبو بكر ناصر بن أبي العباس بن علي الصيدلاني بهراة قالا أنبا محمد بن عبد العزيز الفارسي أنبا عبد الرحمن بن أحمد بن أبي شريح قال نا يحيى بن محمد بن صاعد ثنا أبو سعيد الأشج ثنا عبد الله بن إدريس عن ليث عن مجاهد في قوله عز وجل {فسوف يأتي الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه} قال: قوم سبأ، والأشعريون قوم من سبأ. وأكرم بذلك أصلا ونسبا. أخبرنا الشيخان أبو القاسم عبد الملك بن عبد الله بن داود المغربي وأبو غالب محمد بن الحسن بن علي البصري الماوردي ببغداد قالا أنبا أبو علي علي بن أحمد بن علي التستري بالبصرة ثنا القاضي الشريف أبو عمر
Al-Hamd ibn 'Isa narrated to us: Isma'il ibn bint al-Bisri narrated to us: Husayn ibn 'Isa narrated to us from Ma'mar from al-Zuhri from Abu Hazim from Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, who said: While the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was in Medina, he said: 'Allahu akbar, the help of Allah and the conquest have come, and the people of Yemen have come.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what are the people of Yemen? He said: 'A people with tender hearts, soft in obedience, faith is Yemeni, jurisprudence is Yemeni, wisdom is Yemeni.' Abu Mas'ud 'Abd al-Rahim ibn 'Ali ibn Hamd informed us: Abu 'Ali al-Haddad reported to us: Abu Nu'aym al-Hafiz reported to us: Sulayman ibn Ahmad narrated to us: Ahmad ibn 'Amr al-Qatrani narrated to us: Sulayman ibn Jarb (h). And Abu Nu'aym informed us, saying: al-Ghatrifi narrated to us: Abu Khalifa narrated to us: al-Hawdi narrated to us: they said: Shu'ba narrated to us from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari: When {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} was revealed, the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'They are the people of this one' and struck his hand on the back of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Abu Nu'aym said: Idris al-Awdi narrated it from Simak. The Shaykh Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-Karim ibn Hamza ibn al-Khadir al-Sulami in Damascus informed us: Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz narrated to us: Abu al-Qasim Tamam ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Razi reported to us: my father, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated to us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn al-Ja'd al-Washa' in Baghdad narrated to us: Abu Mu'mar Isma'il ibn Ibrahim al-Qati'i narrated to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from his father from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari who said: It was recited before the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} and he said: 'They are your people, the people of Yemen.' The Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Faqih informed us: Abu Bakr al-Khasrujirdi reported to us: Abu Tahir al-Faqih reported to us: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Saffar reported to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated to us: Abu Mu'mar narrated to me: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from his father from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa who said: It was recited before the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} and the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said to me: 'They are your people, O Abu Musa, the people of Yemen.' The Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi informed us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi al-Hafiz reported to us, saying: To proceed: Some of the Ash'ari imams mentioned to me the text of the hadith which Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us: Abu al-'Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub narrated to us: Ibrahim ibn Marzuq narrated to us: Wahb ibn Jarir and Abu 'Amir al-'Aqadi narrated to us: they said: Shu'ba narrated to us from Simak. And Abu Bakr 'Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirawi informed us in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin 'Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr al-Tabasi in Nishapur narrated to me from him, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Hayri reported to us: Muhammad ibn Ya'qub narrated to us: Ibrahim ibn Marzuq narrated to us: Wahb from Shu'ba narrated to us, and he said: Ibrahim narrated to us: Abu 'Amir from Shu'ba from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari who said: When {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} was revealed, the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, gestured towards Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with him, and said: 'They are the people of this one.' Al-Bayhaqi said: That is because of the great virtue and noble rank found in him for Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, for he is from the people of Abu Musa and his descendants who were given knowledge and granted understanding, distinguished among them by strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation by manifesting proof and refuting doubts. It is more likely that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, only made the people of Abu Musa among the people Allah loves and who love Him because of what he knew of the soundness of their religion and what he recognized of the strength of their certainty. So whoever follows their way in the science of principles (usul) and follows their statement in negating anthropomorphism while adhering to the Book and Sunnah, he is made among their number and counted among their company by the will and permission of Allah. May Allah Almighty help us to that by His grace and seal with happiness and martyrdom by His bounty. And let the fair-minded among our companions know the act of Allah Almighty in presenting this noble origin for what He has stored for His servants of this lofty branch, by which He revived the Sunnah and killed innovation, and made it a true successor to a truthful predecessor. Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn 'Abd Allah al-Misri and Abu Bakr Nasir ibn Abi al-'Abbas ibn 'Ali al-Saydalani in Herat informed us: they said: Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Farisi reported to us: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Shurayh reported to us: Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id narrated to us: Abu Sa'id al-Ashajj narrated to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from Layth from Mujahid regarding His word, exalted: {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} he said: The people of Saba', and the Ash'aris are a people from Saba'. How noble is that origin and lineage! The two shaykhs Abu al-Qasim 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Dawud al-Maghribi and Abu Ghalib Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Basri al-Mawardi in Baghdad informed us: they said: Abu 'Ali 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Tustari in Basra reported to us: the judge al-Sharif Abu 'Umar
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a multi-chain hadith report and scholarly commentary establishing the virtue of the Ash'ari school. It begins with a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas describing the people of Yemen as having tender hearts and being the source of faith, jurisprudence, and wisdom. Then multiple chains from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari report that when the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him' was revealed, the Prophet pointed to Abu Musa and said 'They are the people of this one' or explicitly said 'They are your people, the people of Yemen.' This identifies the 'people Allah loves' as the Ash'aris (descendants of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari). The author then quotes al-Bayhaqi's commentary, which explains that this hadith indicates the great virtue of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who is from the people of Abu Musa, and that the Prophet's statement applies to all who follow the Ash'ari methodology in usul al-din (principles of religion) by negating anthropomorphism (tashbih) while adhering to the Quran and Sunnah. The passage concludes with a chain from Mujahid that the promised people are from Saba', and the Ash'aris are from Saba', thus further ennobling their origin. The overall argument is that the Ash'ari school is rooted in prophetic praise and therefore legitimate and praiseworthy.

Key Terms
الأشعريون
أبو موسى الأشعري
فسوف يأتي الله بقوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people He loves' refers to a future generation unrelated to the Companions.
Correction: The hadiths in this passage show that the Prophet himself identified these people as the Ash'aris of Yemen, specifically pointing to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, a Companion. Thus the verse refers to them.

Checkpoint
In the hadiths, who did the Prophet indicate as the people referred to in the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him'?
A) The Quraysh
B) The people of Yemen, specifically the Ash'aris
C) The Ansar of Medina
D) The Banu Hashim

Key Takeaway
The Prophet directly identified the people Allah loves as the Ash'aris of Yemen, a key proof for the school's virtue.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Prophet specifically identified the Ash'aris as the people Allah loves, do you find yourself grateful to be associated with that group? Or do you feel left out? How does that make you reconsider your own standing with Allah?
?
If Allah loves a specific people for their qualities, what does that mean for you today? What qualities of the Ash'aris (their faith, loyalty) might you need to cultivate to be among those whom Allah loves?
?
The Prophet struck Abu Musa's back and said 'They are the people of this one.' Are you willing to be pointed out as a sign of Allah's love? What would it take for you to be that person?

Sects and Disagreements

Al-Bayhaqi's Commentary and the Ash'ari Lineage
Al-Bayhaqi's commentary and a lineage report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Bayhaqi's explanation of why Imam al-Ash'ari and his followers are included in the prophetic praise, and how the Ash'aris trace their lineage to Saba'.

Core Idea
Imam al-Ash'ari revived the Sunnah by following the path of negating anthropomorphism.

After citing the hadiths, al-Bayhaqi provides a theological commentary explaining that the prophetic praise applies to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and all who follow his methodology in usul al-din—negating tashbih while adhering to the Quran and Sunnah. The lesson also includes a report that the Ash'aris are from the ancient tribe of Saba', further ennobling their origin.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Bayhaqi's commentary
Read the Arabic and translation of al-Bayhaqi's explanation. He connects the hadith directly to Imam al-Ash'ari, noting his virtues.
Al-Bayhaqi was a major Shafi'i-Ash'ari scholar.
2
Identify the key principles
Note the criteria al-Bayhaqi mentions: strengthening the Sunnah, suppressing innovation, negating anthropomorphism (tashbih), and adherence to the Quran and Sunnah.
This defines the Ash'ari methodology.
3
Read the lineage report
Read the final report from Mujahid that traces the Ash'aris to Saba'. Reflect on how this adds to their noble status.
Saba' is an ancient Yemeni tribe with a blessed history.

أبي الحسن الأشعري رضي الله عنه، فهو من قوم أبي موسى وأولاده الذين أوتوا العلم ورزقوا الفهم، مخصوصا من بينهم بتقوية السنة وقمع البدعة بإظهار الحجة ورد الشبهة. والأشبه أن يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إنما جعل قوم أبي موسى من قوم يحبهم الله ويحبونه، لما علم من صحة دينهم وعرف من قوة يقينهم، فمن نحا في علم الأصول نحوهم وتبع في نفي التشبيه مع ملازمة الكتاب والسنة قولهم جعل من جملتهم وعد من حسابهم بمشيئة الله وإذنه. أعاننا الله تعالى على ذلك بمنه وختم بالسعادة والشهادة بجوده. وليعلم المنصف من أصحابنا صنع الله تعالى في تقديم هذا الأصل الشريف لما ذخر لعباده من هذا الفرع المنيف الذي أحيا به السنة وأمات به البدعة، وجعله خلف حق لسلف صدق. أخبرنا أبو الفتح محمد بن علي بن عبد الله المصري وأبو بكر ناصر بن أبي العباس بن علي الصيدلاني بهراة قالا أنبا محمد بن عبد العزيز الفارسي أنبا عبد الرحمن بن أحمد بن أبي شريح قال نا يحيى بن محمد بن صاعد ثنا أبو سعيد الأشج ثنا عبد الله بن إدريس عن ليث عن مجاهد في قوله عز وجل {فسوف يأتي الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه} قال: قوم سبأ، والأشعريون قوم من سبأ. وأكرم بذلك أصلا ونسبا. أخبرنا الشيخان أبو القاسم عبد الملك بن عبد الله بن داود المغربي وأبو غالب محمد بن الحسن بن علي البصري الماوردي ببغداد قالا أنبا أبو علي علي بن أحمد بن علي التستري بالبصرة ثنا القاضي الشريف أبو عمر
Al-Hamd ibn 'Isa narrated to us: Isma'il ibn bint al-Bisri narrated to us: Husayn ibn 'Isa narrated to us from Ma'mar from al-Zuhri from Abu Hazim from Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, who said: While the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was in Medina, he said: 'Allahu akbar, the help of Allah and the conquest have come, and the people of Yemen have come.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what are the people of Yemen? He said: 'A people with tender hearts, soft in obedience, faith is Yemeni, jurisprudence is Yemeni, wisdom is Yemeni.' Abu Mas'ud 'Abd al-Rahim ibn 'Ali ibn Hamd informed us: Abu 'Ali al-Haddad reported to us: Abu Nu'aym al-Hafiz reported to us: Sulayman ibn Ahmad narrated to us: Ahmad ibn 'Amr al-Qatrani narrated to us: Sulayman ibn Jarb (h). And Abu Nu'aym informed us, saying: al-Ghatrifi narrated to us: Abu Khalifa narrated to us: al-Hawdi narrated to us: they said: Shu'ba narrated to us from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari: When {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} was revealed, the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'They are the people of this one' and struck his hand on the back of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Abu Nu'aym said: Idris al-Awdi narrated it from Simak. The Shaykh Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-Karim ibn Hamza ibn al-Khadir al-Sulami in Damascus informed us: Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz narrated to us: Abu al-Qasim Tamam ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Razi reported to us: my father, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated to us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn al-Ja'd al-Washa' in Baghdad narrated to us: Abu Mu'mar Isma'il ibn Ibrahim al-Qati'i narrated to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from his father from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari who said: It was recited before the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} and he said: 'They are your people, the people of Yemen.' The Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Faqih informed us: Abu Bakr al-Khasrujirdi reported to us: Abu Tahir al-Faqih reported to us: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Saffar reported to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated to us: Abu Mu'mar narrated to me: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from his father from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa who said: It was recited before the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} and the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said to me: 'They are your people, O Abu Musa, the people of Yemen.' The Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi informed us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi al-Hafiz reported to us, saying: To proceed: Some of the Ash'ari imams mentioned to me the text of the hadith which Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us: Abu al-'Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub narrated to us: Ibrahim ibn Marzuq narrated to us: Wahb ibn Jarir and Abu 'Amir al-'Aqadi narrated to us: they said: Shu'ba narrated to us from Simak. And Abu Bakr 'Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirawi informed us in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin 'Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr al-Tabasi in Nishapur narrated to me from him, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Hayri reported to us: Muhammad ibn Ya'qub narrated to us: Ibrahim ibn Marzuq narrated to us: Wahb from Shu'ba narrated to us, and he said: Ibrahim narrated to us: Abu 'Amir from Shu'ba from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari who said: When {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} was revealed, the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, gestured towards Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with him, and said: 'They are the people of this one.' Al-Bayhaqi said: That is because of the great virtue and noble rank found in him for Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, for he is from the people of Abu Musa and his descendants who were given knowledge and granted understanding, distinguished among them by strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation by manifesting proof and refuting doubts. It is more likely that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, only made the people of Abu Musa among the people Allah loves and who love Him because of what he knew of the soundness of their religion and what he recognized of the strength of their certainty. So whoever follows their way in the science of principles (usul) and follows their statement in negating anthropomorphism while adhering to the Book and Sunnah, he is made among their number and counted among their company by the will and permission of Allah. May Allah Almighty help us to that by His grace and seal with happiness and martyrdom by His bounty. And let the fair-minded among our companions know the act of Allah Almighty in presenting this noble origin for what He has stored for His servants of this lofty branch, by which He revived the Sunnah and killed innovation, and made it a true successor to a truthful predecessor. Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn 'Abd Allah al-Misri and Abu Bakr Nasir ibn Abi al-'Abbas ibn 'Ali al-Saydalani in Herat informed us: they said: Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Farisi reported to us: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Shurayh reported to us: Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id narrated to us: Abu Sa'id al-Ashajj narrated to us: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from Layth from Mujahid regarding His word, exalted: {Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him} he said: The people of Saba', and the Ash'aris are a people from Saba'. How noble is that origin and lineage! The two shaykhs Abu al-Qasim 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Dawud al-Maghribi and Abu Ghalib Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Basri al-Mawardi in Baghdad informed us: they said: Abu 'Ali 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Tustari in Basra reported to us: the judge al-Sharif Abu 'Umar
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a multi-chain hadith report and scholarly commentary establishing the virtue of the Ash'ari school. It begins with a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas describing the people of Yemen as having tender hearts and being the source of faith, jurisprudence, and wisdom. Then multiple chains from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari report that when the verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people He loves and who love Him' was revealed, the Prophet pointed to Abu Musa and said 'They are the people of this one' or explicitly said 'They are your people, the people of Yemen.' This identifies the 'people Allah loves' as the Ash'aris (descendants of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari). The author then quotes al-Bayhaqi's commentary, which explains that this hadith indicates the great virtue of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who is from the people of Abu Musa, and that the Prophet's statement applies to all who follow the Ash'ari methodology in usul al-din (principles of religion) by negating anthropomorphism (tashbih) while adhering to the Quran and Sunnah. The passage concludes with a chain from Mujahid that the promised people are from Saba', and the Ash'aris are from Saba', thus further ennobling their origin. The overall argument is that the Ash'ari school is rooted in prophetic praise and therefore legitimate and praiseworthy.

Key Terms
نفي التشبيه
علم الأصول
سبأ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bayhaqi, what qualifies a person to be included in the prophetic praise of the people Allah loves?
A) Being a direct descendant of Abu Musa
B) Following the Ash'ari methodology in usul al-din, negating anthropomorphism and adhering to Quran and Sunnah
C) Living in Yemen
D) Memorizing the entire Quran

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari methodology of negating anthropomorphism while adhering to Quran and Sunnah is the true inheritor of the prophetic praise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this lesson, al-Bayhaqi emphasizes that the prophetic praise is for those who follow the Ash'ari methodology of negating anthropomorphism. Do you actively examine your understanding of Allah's attributes to ensure you are free from any form of tashbih? Take a moment to reflect on a specific attribute of Allah (e.g., His Hand, His Face) and ask yourself: have I ever imagined it in a way that resembles creation? Commit today to learning the correct understanding from the Quran and Sunnah as interpreted by the righteous scholars.
?
The passage highlights that the praise is not merely for a tribe but for anyone who adheres to the correct methodology. Consider your own religious identity: do you place more confidence in your family background, sect, or school than in your actual adherence to the truth? This lesson calls you to prioritize substance over association. Repent for any pride in lineage and resolve to follow the methodology that pleases Allah.

Defending the Renewers: al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani
Ibn Asakir discusses alternative opinions on the renewers and defends al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing views on who renewed the faith at the 300th and 400th Hijri years and why Ibn Asakir favors al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani.

Core Idea
Not all renewer lists agree; Ibn Asakir champions al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir continues his discussion of the mujaddid tradition by presenting alternative views. He argues for the correctness of al-Ash'ari for the third century and al-Baqillani for the fourth, providing reasons based on their contributions to defending orthodoxy. The passage also sheds light on the role of the al-Sa'luki family in spreading Ash'arism and refutes slander against al-Ash'ari.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claims
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Identify the two main claims: who is proposed as the renewer for 300 AH and 400 AH.
Note that Ibn Asakir mentions alternative opinions before giving his preference.
2
Analyze Ibn Asakir's reasons
For each century, note the reasons Ibn Asakir gives for preferring al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani. What makes them more deserving according to him?
Look for phrases like 'أصوب' (more correct) and 'أولى' (more worthy).
3
Observe the treatment of alternatives
Notice how Ibn Asakir acknowledges the merits of Ibn Surayj and Abu al-Tayyib. Then see how he uses Abu al-Tayyib's praise of al-Ash'ari to refute al-Ahwazi's accusation.
This shows scholarly objectivity and defense against sectarian attacks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر غير الفقيه ابى الحسن ان ابا العباس أحمد ابن عمر بن سريج الفقيه هو الذى كان على رأس الثلثمائة وان ابا الطيب سهل بن محمد بن سليمان الصعلوكي النيسابوري هو الذي كان على . رأس الاربعمائة، وقول من قال انه أبو الحسن الأشعری اصوب لأن قيامه بنصرة السنة إلى تجديد الدين أقرب فهو الذي انتدب للرد على المعتزلة وسائر اصناف المبتدعة المضللة وحالته فى ذلك مشتهرة وكتبه في الرد عليهم منتشرة، فأما أبو العباس بن سريج فكان فقيها مضطلعا بعلم اصول الفقه وفروعه نبيها وقول من قال ان القاضى ابا بكر محمد بن الطيب الباقلاني هو الذى كان على رأس الاربعمائة اولى من القول الثاني لأنه اشهر من أبي الطيب الصعلوكى مكانا وأعلى فى رتب القوم شانا وذكره اكبر من أكثر من محمد بن بن عدی ان ينكر وقدره أظهر من ان يستر وتصانيفه اشهر من ان تشهر وتواليفه ان تذكر، فاما أبو الطيب رحمه الله فانما اشتهر ذكره ببلده وكانت رياسة اصحاب الشافعي له بنيسابور ولوالده ولولده وكان ابوه أبو سهل محمد بن سليمان رحمه الله ذا محل خطير، وذكره فيما بين أهل العلم خراسان كبير لم يزل هو وولده وولد ولده يظهرون مذهب الأشعرية ويجاهدون اهل البدع بنيسابور من المعتزلة والرافضة والكرامية، وما تقدم من قوله في مدح الأشعرى مما رواه عنه أبو عمرو الرزجاهي يدل على كذب ابي على الاهوازي فيما حكى عنه اذ رماه باحدى الدواهي
And someone other than the jurist Abu al-Hasan mentioned that Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Umar ibn Surayj al-Faqih was the one at the head of three hundred, and that Abu al-Tayyib Sahl ibn Muhammad ibn Sulayman al-Sa'luki al-Naysaburi was the one at the head of four hundred. And the statement of those who said that he is Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is more correct, because his standing up for the support of the Sunnah is closer to the renewal of religion. He is the one who dedicated himself to refuting the Mu'tazila and all the deviant innovator sects; his state in that is well-known and his books in refutation of them are widespread. As for Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj, he was a jurist, proficient in the science of usul al-fiqh and its branches, intelligent. And the statement of those who said that the Qadi Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Tayyib al-Baqillani was the one at the head of four hundred is more worthy than the second statement, because he is more famous than Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luki in standing, higher in rank among the people, and his renown is greater than can be denied, his worth more apparent than to be concealed, his treatises too famous to be publicized, and his writings need not be mentioned. As for Abu al-Tayyib, may Allah have mercy on him, his fame was only in his own country, and he had the leadership of the Shafi'i scholars in Nishapur, as did his father and his son. His father Abu Sahl Muhammad ibn Sulayman, may Allah have mercy on him, was of great station, and his reputation among the people of knowledge in Khurasan was great. He, his son, and his grandson continued to manifest the Ash'ari school and struggle against the people of innovation in Nishapur, namely the Mu'tazila, the Rafidah, and the Karramiyya. And what was mentioned earlier of his statement in praise of al-Ash'ari, narrated by Abu Amr al-Razjahi, indicates the falsehood of Abu Ali al-Ahwazi in what he reported about him, when he accused him of one of the calamities.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the mujaddid tradition, presenting alternative opinions. The author reports that some say Ibn Surayj was at the head of the 300th year and Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luki at the 400th. However, Ibn Asakir argues that al-Ash'ari is more correct for the third century because his defense of the Sunnah is more pertinent to the renewal of religion; he actively refuted the Mu'tazila and other deviant sects, and his works are widespread. For the fourth century, he prefers al-Baqillani over Abu al-Tayyib, giving reasons: al-Baqillani is more famous, higher in rank, and his writings are too well-known to need mention. He then acknowledges the merits of Abu al-Tayyib and his family as Ash'ari supporters in Nishapur, fighting innovations. Finally, he uses the earlier praise of al-Ash'ari to refute the slander of Abu Ali al-Ahwazi, showing that the positive statements from al-Sa'luki prove the falsehood of al-Ahwazi's accusations.

Key Terms
ابن سريج
أبو الطيب الصعلوكي
الأشعري
الباقلاني
المعتزلة
الرافضة
الكرامية
أبو علي الاهوازي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people claimed that al-Ash'ari was a heretic based on reports from Abu Ali al-Ahwazi.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that even those who were not al-Ash'ari (like Abu al-Tayyib) praised him, proving the accusation false.

Checkpoint
Why does Ibn Asakir prefer al-Ash'ari over Ibn Surayj for the third century?
A) Because al-Ash'ari was older
B) Because al-Ash'ari defended the Sunnah and refuted heretics
C) Because Ibn Surayj was not a scholar
D) Because al-Ash'ari wrote more books

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir defends the Ash'ari school by asserting that al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani are the true renewers of their centuries, based on their defense of orthodoxy and widespread influence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative report about a scholar of Ahl al-Sunnah, do you immediately accept it or do you seek to verify, as Ibn Asakir does by citing praise from others? How will you change your approach starting today?
?
The passage shows al-Ash'ari dedicated himself to refuting deviant sects. Are you willing to speak out against falsehoods in your own environment, even at personal cost? What is one step you can take this week to support the truth?
?
Ibn Asakir defends al-Baqillani as more worthy of the title of renewer due to his wider influence. In your own life, are you seeking to have a broad beneficial impact for the deen, or are you content with limited fame? What practical steps can you take to increase your contribution?

Bilal's Severity against the People of Desires
Ibn 'Asakir reports Bilal's severity and its legacy in al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Bilal ibn Abi Burda's strictness against heretical innovations was inherited by his descendant Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, shaping his cautious theological approach.

Core Idea
Bilal's severity against heretics left a legacy of caution that influenced al-Ash'ari.

This lesson presents a historical report from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin, showing how the early Muslim governor Bilal ibn Abi Burda was known for his harsh treatment of those with innovated beliefs. Remarkably, this trait was inherited by his descendant, the great theologian Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who became cautious in dealing with theological diseases.

Guided Path
1
Read the appointment report
Start by reading the part where Bilal is appointed over Basra and his duties are listed. Notice his severity against 'ahl al-ahwa'.
The chain of narrators is long but authentic in the tradition.
2
Identify the inheritance
Pay attention to the phrase 'fa awratha dhalika 'aqabahu' – this severity passed to his descendants. Then see how it connects to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
Al-Ash'ari is described as 'waqqaf' (cautious) among them.
3
Reflect on the metaphor
The term 'adwa'' (diseases) is used for innovations. Consider why heresy is likened to a disease and why caution is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندي أنا أبو الحسين أحمد بن محمد بن النقور والقاضي أبو منصور عبد الباقي بن محمد بن غالب بن العطار قالا أنا أبو طاهر محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن العباس المخلص أنا أبو محمد عبيد الله بن عبد الرحمن بن عيسى السكري نا أبو يعلى زكريا بن يحيى النقري نا الأصمعي نا بن بلال عن مجالد قال ثم ولي العراق خالد بن عبد الله القسري فكان على شرطته بواسط عمرو بن عبد الأعلى الحكمي واستعمل على الكوفة العريان بن الهيثم واستعمل على البصرة مالك بن المنذر بن الجارود العبدي ثم عزله واستعمل بلال بن أبي بردة فكان على الأحداث والصلاة والقضاء وكان بلال بن أبي بردة شديدا على أهل الأهواء فأورث ذلك عقبه. فكان أبو الحسن وقافا منهم على الأدواء. كذلك أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن الفضل بن أحمد الفراوي أخبرنا أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن محمد بن عبد الغافر الفارسي أنا أبو سليمان حمد بن محمد بن إبراهيم الخطابي البستي أخبرني أحمد بن إبراهيم بن مالك نا الدغولي يعني أبا العباس محمد بن عبد الرحمن السرخسي نا المظفري يعني محمد بن حاتم نا أبو بهز بن أبي الخطاب السلمي قال: كان زريع أبو يزيد بن زريع على عسس بلال بن أبي بردة قال فقال له بلغني أن أهل الأهواء يجتمعون في المسجد ويتنازعون فاذهب فتعرف ذلك قال فذهب ثم رجع إليه فقال ما وجدت فيه إلا أهل العربية حلقة حلقة فقال ألا جلست إليهم حتى لا تقول حلقة حلقة قال أبو سليمان الخطابي وإنما هي الحلقة حلقة القوم وحلقة القرط ونحوها أخبرني أبو عمرو أنا ثعلب عن عمرو بن أبي عمرو الشيباني عن أبيه قال لا أقول حلقة إلا في جمع حالق.
And the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Naqur and al-Qadi Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Baqi ibn Muhammad ibn Ghalib ibn al-'Attar informed us, both saying: Abu Tahir Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-'Abbas al-Mukhlis informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad 'Ubayd Allah ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Isa al-Sukkari informed us, saying: Abu Ya'la Zakariyya ibn Yahya al-Naqri narrated to us, saying: al-Asma'i narrated to us, saying: Ibn Bilal narrated from Mujalid, saying: Then Khalid ibn 'Abd Allah al-Qasri took charge of Iraq; his police chief in Wasit was 'Amr ibn 'Abd al-A'la al-Hakami; he appointed over Kufa al-'Uryan ibn al-Haytham; and he appointed over Basra Malik ibn al-Mundhir ibn al-Jarud al-'Abdi; then he dismissed him and appointed Bilal ibn Abi Burda, so he was in charge of the young men, prayer, and judiciary. And Bilal ibn Abi Burda was severe against the people of desires (ahl al-ahwa'), and that passed on to his descendants. So Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari) was cautious among them regarding diseases. Similarly, the shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl ibn Ahmad al-Farawi informed us, saying: Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-Ghafir ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi informed us, saying: Abu Sulayman Hamd ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Khattabi al-Busti informed us, saying: Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Malik informed me, saying: al-Daghuli (meaning Abu al-'Abbas Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sarakhsi) narrated to us, saying: al-Muzafari (meaning Muhammad ibn Hatim) narrated to us, saying: Abu Bahz ibn Abi al-Khattab al-Sulami narrated to us, saying: Zuraiq, Abu Yazid ibn Zuraiq, was in charge of the night patrol of Bilal ibn Abi Burda. He said: He said to him: It has reached me that the people of desires gather in the mosque and argue, so go and find out about that. He said: So he went, then returned to him and said: I found no one there except people of Arabic (tongues) sitting in circles (halqa halqa). He said: Why did you not sit with them so that you would not say halqa halqa? Abu Sulayman al-Khattabi said: It is only al-halqa (with sukun) for the circle of people and the ring of an earring and the like. Abu 'Amr informed me: Tha'lab narrated from 'Amr ibn Abi 'Amr al-Shaybani from his father, saying: I do not say halqa (plural) except for the plural of a barber (haliq).
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage contains two reports. First, through al-Asma'i from Mujalid, it narrates that when Khalid al-Qasri governed Iraq, he appointed Bilal ibn Abi Burda over Basra after dismissing Malik ibn al-Mundhir. Bilal was put in charge of the youth, prayer, and judiciary, and he was very severe against the ahl al-ahwa' (people of innovated desires). This severity, the text notes, was inherited by his descendants, so that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (being a descendant) was cautious (waqqaf) among them regarding 'adwa' (diseases of innovation). The second report is from Abu Sulayman al-Khattabi via a different chain. It tells that Zuraiq, the father of Yazid ibn Zuraiq, was the head of Bilal's night patrol. Bilal heard that heretics gathered in the mosque to debate, so he sent Zuraiq to investigate. Zuraiq returned and reported only finding people studying Arabic in circles (halqa). Bilal corrected his pronunciation: 'halqa' (with sukun on lam) is correct, not 'halqa' (with fatha). Al-Khattabi then provides a linguistic note: al-halqa (with sukun) is used for a circle of people, an earring ring, etc. He then quotes Tha'lab's authority that he only says 'halqa' (pronounced with fatha) for the plural of a barber (haliq). The story demonstrates Bilal's vigilance against heresy even in small details, and the linguistic correction shows scholarly precision.

Key Terms
أهل الأهواء
أبو الحسن الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the inheritance of Bilal's severity?
A) Wealth and property
B) A strict approach to governance
C) Caution against heretical diseases in his descendant al-Ash'ari
D) A reputation for harsh punishment

Key Takeaway
Bilal's severity against heretics was not just personal but became a hereditary caution that al-Ash'ari embodied in his theological work.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says Bilal's severity passed to his descendants. Are you inheriting a severity against falsehood from your predecessors, or have you grown lax? Where do you draw the line?
?
Al-Ash'ari was cautious regarding 'diseases' of innovation. What 'diseases' of belief or practice are you tolerating in your own life? Will you commit to identifying one such disease today and cutting it out?
?
Bilal was severe against people of desires. Do you treat your own desires with the same severity? How do you respond when your soul desires something that contradicts the truth?

The Halqa Story: Linguistic Precision in Guarding Orthodoxy
Ibn 'Asakir reports a story illustrating Bilal's attention to linguistic precision in guarding orthodoxy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a small linguistic correction in a story about heretics illustrates the meticulous attention to detail among early Muslim scholars.

Core Idea
A simple pronunciation correction reveals the depth of scholarly care in preserving orthodoxy.

This lesson presents a vivid anecdote from the life of Bilal ibn Abi Burda. He sends his night patrol chief to investigate reports of heretics gathering in the mosque. The chief finds only Arabic study circles and reports using the word 'halqa' with a fatha. Bilal corrects him, showing that even the smallest detail matters in guarding the faith. The passage then provides a linguistic note from al-Khattabi on the correct pronunciation.

Guided Path
1
Read the story
Start by reading the second report, where Bilal sends Zuraiq to check the mosque. Notice the report of 'halqa halqa' (circles).
The chain is different from the first report but also authentic.
2
Understand the correction
Bilal corrects Zuraiq's pronunciation: 'Why did you not sit with them so that you would not say halqa halqa?' This implies the correct word is 'halqa' with sukun.
Note that Bilal's concern is both theological and linguistic.
3
Review the linguistic explanation
Al-Khattabi explains that 'al-halqa' (sukun) is used for a circle of people and a ring. He then quotes Tha'lab, who says 'halqa' (fatha) is only used for the plural of a barber.
This shows the depth of linguistic scholarship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'halqa' with fatha is correct for a circle of people.
Correction: The correct word for a circle is 'al-halqa' with sukun on the lam; 'halqa' with fatha is only used for the plural of 'barber'.

?

?
Bilal was vigilant about protecting the mosque from heretical debates. Are you vigilant about the sources of your own knowledge? Do you verify what you learn from social media or casual conversations? What step will you take tomorrow to verify one thing you think you know about Islam?

From Prohibition to Duty: The Evolution of Debating Innovators
Ibn Asakir explains the need to debate innovators and cites hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early Salaf avoided debating innovators and why later scholars like Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari engaged in it, and two hadiths that guide this practice.

Core Idea
The duty to debate innovation changes with time: from avoidance to necessity.

The early Muslim community (Salaf) considered debating innovators harmful, even citing a hadith against sitting with them. Yet later, when innovations spread widely, the same tradition commanded defending the truth. This lesson explores the historical shift and the two hadiths that define the boundaries of theological debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the full Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of the author's argument and the two hadiths cited.
Pay attention to the flow: first the prohibition, then the justification for debating later.
2
Identify the early position of the Salaf
Notice that the author states the Salaf considered debating innovators 'wrong and foolish.' Understand why Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari initially opposed it.
The first hadith prohibits even sitting with people of Qadr.
3
Examine the shift in circumstances
See the turning point: when innovations became widespread and threatened the common people, the imams stepped up to debate and refute them.
This is a key point: duty changes with need.
4
Study the second hadith on divine guardians
Read the second hadith promising that Allah appoints a guardian for every innovation. Understand how it supports the necessity of debating.
This hadith legitimizes the new practice.
5
Synthesize the two hadiths
Consider how the two hadiths together guide the approach: avoid unnecessary debate, but defend when truth is endangered.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الامام الحافظ رضى الله عنه وانما سمى أبو الحسن رحمه الله مناظرة المعتزلة بدعة وكرهها، لأن السلف كانوا يرون مكالمة أهل البدع ومناظرتهم خطأ، وسفها، وقد جاء عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في النهي عن ذلك ما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو سهل محمد بن ابراهيم بن محمد بن سعدويه المزكي الأصبهاني ببغداد أنا أبو القاسم ابراهيم بن منصور بن ابراهيم السلمى انا أبو بكر محمد بن ابراهيم بن على بن عاصم بن المقرى انا أبو يعلى احمد بن على بن المثنى الموصلى نا أبو خيثمة وهرون بن معروف وغيرهما قالوا نا عبد الله بن يزيد المقرى نا سعيد بن أبي أيوب عن عطاء بن دينار عن حكيم بن شريك عن يحيى بن ميمون الحضرمي عن ربيعة الجرشي عن أبي هريرة رضى الله عنه عن عمر رضي الله عنه قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول ( لا تجالســوا أهل القدر ولا تفاتحوهم) قال الحافظ الله عنه فلما ظهرت فيما بعد أقوال أهل البدع واشتهرت وعظمت البلوى بفتنتهم على أهل السنة وانتشرت انتدب للرد عليهم ومناظرتهم أئمة أهل السنة لما خافوا على العوام من الابتداع والفتنة كفعل ابي الحسن رحمه الله واشباهه خوفا من التباس الحق على الخلق، واشتباهه وفى هذا المعنى ورد ما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو على الحسن بن على المقرى فى كتابه وحدثني به الشيخ أبو مسعود عبدالرحيم بن علی بن احمد عنه انا أبو نعيم احمد بن عبدالله الحافظ نا احمد بن اسحق وعبدالله وعبد الرحمن ابنا محمد بن جعفر قالوا انا محمد بن العباس نا زكريا بن الصلت نا أبو الصلت الهروى وأخبرنا أبو البركات عبدالوهاب بن المبارك ابن احمد الأنماطى ببغداد انا أبو بكر محمد بن المظفر بن بكران الشامي انا أبو الحسن احمد بن محمد العتيق انا يوسف بن احمد بن يوسف ابن الدخيل نا أبو جعفر محمد بن عمرو العقیلی نا محمد بن أيوب بن الضريس نا عبدالسلام بن صالح وهو أبو الصلت ناعباد بن العوام نا عبد الغفار المدنى عن سعيد بن المسيب عن أبي هريرة رضى الله عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى صلى الله عليه وسلم ( إن الله عند كل بدعة كيد بها الإسلام وليا يذب عنه ويتكلم بعلاماته فاغتنموا تلك المجالس بالذب عن الضعفاء وتوكلوا على الله وكفى بالله وكيلا) لفظهما سواء.
The imam al-Hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, only called debating the Mu'tazila an innovation and disliked it, because the Salaf considered speaking to and debating the people of innovation to be wrong and foolish. And it has come from the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding the prohibition of that, what was narrated to us by the Shaykh Abu Sahl Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'duwayh al-Muzakki al-Isbahani in Baghdad, who said: Abu al-Qasim Ibrahim ibn Mansur ibn Ibrahim al-Sulami narrated to us, who said: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Asim ibn al-Muqri' narrated to us, who said: Abu Ya'la Ahmad ibn Ali ibn al-Muthanna al-Mawsili narrated to us, who said: Abu Khaythama and Harun ibn Ma'ruf and others narrated to us, who said: Abdullah ibn Yazid al-Muqri' narrated to us, who said: Sa'id ibn Abi Ayyub narrated to us from Ata ibn Dinar from Hakim ibn Sharik from Yahya ibn Maymun al-Hadrami from Rabi'a al-Jurashi from Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, from Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'Do not sit with the people of Qadr and do not initiate conversation with them.' The Hafiz said: Then later when the statements of the people of innovation appeared, became well-known, and the trial of their fitna upon Ahl al-Sunna became great and spread, the imams of Ahl al-Sunna stepped forward to refute them and debate them, out of fear for the common people of innovation and fitna, like the action of Abu al-Hasan and his peers, out of fear that the truth would be confused for the people and become ambiguous. And in this meaning is what was narrated to us by the Shaykh Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Muqri' in his book, and the Shaykh Abu Mas'ud Abd al-Rahim ibn Ali ibn Ahmad narrated it to me from him, who said: Abu Nu'aym Ahmad ibn Abdullah al-Hafiz narrated to us, who said: Ahmad ibn Ishaq and Abdullah and Abd al-Rahman, the two sons of Muhammad ibn Ja'far, narrated to us, who said: Muhammad ibn al-Abbas narrated to us, who said: Zakariya ibn al-Salt narrated to us, who said: Abu al-Salt al-Harawi narrated to us, and Abu al-Barakat Abd al-Wahhab ibn al-Mubarak ibn Ahmad al-Anmati in Baghdad narrated to us, who said: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Muzaffar ibn Bakran al-Shami narrated to us, who said: Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Atiq narrated to us, who said: Yusuf ibn Ahmad ibn Yusuf ibn al-Dakhil narrated to us, who said: Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Amr al-Uqayli narrated to us, who said: Muhammad ibn Ayyub ibn al-Durays narrated to us, who said: Abd al-Salam ibn Salih, who is Abu al-Salt, narrated to us, from Abbad ibn al-Awwam, from Abd al-Ghaffar al-Madani, from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, from Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed, for every innovation by which Islam is plotted against, Allah appoints a guardian who defends it and speaks with its signs. So seize those gatherings to defend the weak and rely on Allah, and sufficient is Allah as a Trustee.' Their wording is the same.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is an argument justifying the practice of debating innovators. It begins by stating that the early Salaf considered debating and speaking to people of innovation as wrong and foolish, and the author cites a hadith prohibiting even sitting with the Qadariyya and initiating conversation with them. However, the author then explains that when later innovations spread widely and threatened the common people, the imams of Ahl al-Sunna, including Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, took up the task of debating and refuting them out of fear that the truth would be confused. The author then brings a second hadith with a full chain that promises that for every innovation, Allah appoints a guardian to defend the truth. This indicates that the debate against innovation is not only a response to necessity but also a divine ordering. The phrase 'لفظهما سواء' indicates that both chains transmit the same wording of the second hadith.

Key Terms
بدعة
معتزلة
سلف
أهل القدر
أهل البدع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think debating innovators is always prohibited regardless of circumstances.
Correction: This passage shows that while early Muslims avoided debate, later when innovations spread and threatened the common people, it became a duty to defend the truth through debate.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in the passage, what did the Prophet prohibit regarding people of Qadr?
A) Marrying them
B) Conducting business with them
C) Sitting with them and initiating conversation
D) Eating their food

Key Takeaway
The early prohibition against debating innovators gave way to a duty to defend the truth when innovations threatened the community, as affirmed by the second hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a fellow Muslim spreading ideas you believe are wrong, does your first impulse match the early Salaf (to avoid) or the later imams (to engage)? How does this lesson challenge your default response?
?
The hadith promises that Allah raises guardians for every innovation. Are you currently acting as such a guardian, or are you silent while falsehood spreads? What concrete step will you take this week to defend the weak?
?
If you were living in the time when the Salaf avoided debate, would you have accepted that ruling without question? Now that you know it changed, how do you determine which phase you are in today?

Ibn Asakir's Defense of al-Ash'ari: Context and Intention
Ibn Asakir describes the ruler's actions and states his intention to defend al-Ash'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical and sectarian context that motivated Ibn Asakir to write a defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Ibn Asakir's praise of the ruler is a strategic move to defend al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy.

In this opening section of his work, Ibn Asakir sets the stage by describing the ruler's actions against innovation and the distress this causes to Sunnis. He then reveals his purpose: to clarify the true status of al-Ash'ari and motivate the ruler to defend him. This passage shows how historical and political circumstances shaped theological defense.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the full Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the flow: from praise of the ruler to distress of Sunnis, then to hope of rectification and introduction of al-Ash'ari.
Pay attention to the hadith and Ibn al-Mubarak's statement at the beginning.
2
Identify the key actors and their roles
The ruler is presented as just and powerful. The enemies are innovators (ahl al-bid'a) and deviant sects (Mu'tazila, Mujassima). The Sunnis (Hanafis, Malikis, Shafi'is) are distressed by the cursing. Ibn Asakir expresses hope that the ruler will correct the situation.
3
Understand the strategic purpose of the praise
The praise is not mere flattery; it sets a basis for Ibn Asakir to later argue that al-Ash'ari and his followers are true Sunnis who should be protected. Ask yourself: Why does Ibn Asakir describe the ruler as just and then mention al-Ash'ari's merits?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسلم ( يوم من أيام امام عادل افضل من عبادة ستين سنة ) وقال عبدالله بن المبارك رضى الله عنه : لولا الأئمة لم تأمن لنا سبل وكان أضعفنا نهبا لأقوانا زاده الله علوا وتأييدا وزاد من يؤازره بالخير ويحثه عليه توفيقا وتسديدا، ثم انه اعز الله نصره صرف همته العالية الى نصرة دين الله وقمع اعداء الله بعد ماتقرر للكافة حسن اعتقاده بتقرير خطباء أهل مملكته على لعن من استوجب اللعن من أهل البدعة ببدعته وأيس أهل الزيغ عن زيغه عن الحق وميله عن القصد فألقوا في سمعه مافيه مساءة أهل السنة والجماعة عامة الحنفية والماليكة والشافعية، الذين لا يذهبون في كافة ومصيبتهم من التعطيل مذاهب المعتزلة ولا يسلكون فى التشبيه طرق المجسمة في مشارق الأرض ومغاربها ليتسلوا بالأسوة معهم في هذه المساءة عما يسوءهم من اللعن والقمع في هذه الدولة المنصورة ثبتها الله ، ونحن نرجر عثوره عن قريب على ماقصدوا ووقوفه على ما أرادوا فيستدرك بتوفيق الله عز وجل ما بدر منه فيما ألقى الله ويأمر بتعزير من زور عليه وقبح صورة الأئمة بين يديه، وكأنه خفى عليه أدام الله عزه حال شيخنا أبي الحسن الأشعري رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه وما يرجع إليه من شرف الأصل وكبر المحل في العلم والفضل وكثرة الأصحاب من الحنفية والمالكية والشافعية الذين رغبوا في علم الأصول، وأحبوا معرفة دلائل العقول والشيخ العميد أدام الله توفيقه أولى أوليائه وأحراهم بتعريفه حاله وإعلامه فضله لما يرجع اليه من الهداية والدراية والشهامة والكفاية، مع صحة العقيدة وحسن الطريقة وفضائل الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعرى ومناقبه أكثر من أن يمكن ذكرها في هذه الرسالة لما في الإطالة من خشية الملالة لكنى اذكر بمشيئة الله تعالى من شرفه بآبائه واجداده وفضله بعلمه وحسن اعتقاده وكبر محله بكثرة أصحابه ما يحمله على الذب عنه وعن اتباعه
And he said peace be upon him: 'A day with a just imam is better than sixty years of worship.' And Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Were it not for the imams, our paths would not be safe for us, and the weakest of us would be prey for the strongest of us.' May Allah increase him in highness and support, and increase whoever supports him in goodness and urges him towards it with success and guidance. Then he — may Allah strengthen his victory — directed his high resolve towards supporting the religion of Allah and suppressing the enemies of Allah, after his good belief was established for all through the decree of the preachers of his kingdom to curse whoever deserved cursing among the people of innovation due to his innovation, and the people of deviation despaired of their deviation from the truth and their turning away from moderation. So they cast into his ears what contains displeasure for the people of the Sunnah and the community, generally the Hanafis, Malikis, and Shafi'is, who in all their calamities from ta'til do not follow the ways of the Mu'tazila, nor do they follow in tashbih the ways of the Mujassima in the east of the earth and its west, so that they might console themselves with fellowship with them in this displeasure against what displeases them of cursing and suppression in this victorious state — may Allah establish it. And we are hopeful that he will soon stumble upon what they intended and stop at what they wanted, and he will remedy, with the success of Allah Almighty, what escaped him regarding what Allah cast, and he will order the punishment of those who forged lies against him and defamed the image of the imams in his presence. It is as if it were hidden from him — may Allah prolong his honor — the state of our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, and what pertains to him of nobility of origin, greatness of standing in knowledge and virtue, and the multitude of companions from the Hanafis, Malikis, and Shafi'is who desired the science of principles and loved to know the proofs of intellects. And the respected shaykh — may Allah continue his success — is most worthy of his allies and most deserving of being informed of his state and being told of his virtue, for what pertains to him of guidance, knowledge, chivalry, and sufficiency, along with soundness of creed and goodness of way. And the virtues of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his merits are more than can be mentioned in this epistle due to fear of boredom from length. But I will mention, by the will of Allah Almighty, from his nobility through his fathers and grandfathers, and his virtue through his knowledge and good belief, and his great standing through the multitude of his companions, what will motivate him to defend him and his followers.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a combination of praise for the ruler and an explanation of the context that prompts Ibn Asakir to defend Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It begins by citing a hadith about the virtue of a just imam and the statement of Ibn al-Mubarak about the necessity of imams. Then it describes how the ruler, after establishing his orthodoxy, ordered the cursing of innovators, which caused distress to the Sunnis who follow the Hanafi, Maliki, and Shafi'i schools — those who avoid the ta'til of the Mu'tazila and the tashbih of the Mujassima. Ibn Asakir expresses hope that the ruler will realize the true state of al-Ash'ari and retract any harm done. He then launches into a eulogy of al-Ash'ari, mentioning his noble origin, his high station in knowledge, and his many followers who are students of usul al-din and rational proofs. The passage concludes with Ibn Asakir's intention to mention al-Ash'ari's lineage and virtues to motivate the ruler to defend him. The overall function is to set the stage for the biographical and doctrinal defense that follows.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
المعتزلة
المجسمة
أهل البدعة
أصول الدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Ibn Asakir's praise of the ruler is merely flattery to gain personal favor.
Correction: The praise is a strategic rhetorical device to establish the ruler's justice and then argue that al-Ash'ari and his followers—who are the true Sunnis—deserve protection, as they are being harmed by the ruler's policy against innovation.

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of Ibn Asakir's praise of the ruler at the beginning of this passage?
A) To flatter the ruler and seek personal favor
B) To establish the context of why defending al-Ash'ari is necessary
C) To criticize the ruler for cursing innovators
D) To list the virtues of just imams

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir's defense of al-Ash'ari is rooted in the political and sectarian context of his time, where the ruler's actions against innovation inadvertently harmed Sunnis, prompting a clarification of al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself unknowingly supporting a cause that harmed the truth because you listened to slander instead of seeking the truth yourself? What will you do to ensure you are not like the ruler in this passage?
?
Ibn Asakir had the courage to stand up for what he knew was true even when the ruler was against it. Is there an unpopular truth in your community that you are avoiding defending? What is holding you back?
?
The passage shows that the people of innovation used slander to turn the ruler against Sunnis. Are there people today who spread falsehoods about those who hold correct beliefs? What is your responsibility when you hear such slander?
