Unity of Sunni Scholars and the Role of Just Rulers
Ibn Asakir affirms the unity of Sunni scholars, the Ash'ari consensus on usul, and the dependence on just rulers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir affirms the unity of Sunni scholars, particularly the Ash'aris, and the importance of righteous leadership in safeguarding orthodox theology.

Core Idea
Sunni scholars are united; the community's well-being depends on just rulers.

Ibn Asakir, in his defense of Ash'ari theology, emphasizes that Sunni scholars are not divided but united, and the Ash'aris are part of that consensus. He then turns to a crucial practical point: the uprightness of the community's conditions depends on the uprightness of its rulers. He supports this with the sayings of Umar ibn al-Khattab and Abu Hazim, warning that when heretical desires influence rulers, the people lose their protectors.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
Pay attention to the chains of transmission which indicate the reliability of the quotes.
2
Identify the two main claims
Notice that Ibn Asakir first states the unity of Sunni scholars and Ash'ari agreement on usul. Then he introduces the conditional relationship between the uprightness of scholars and rulers.
This is a shift from doctrinal unity to socio-political necessity.
3
Examine the evidence from Umar and Abu Hazim
Read the quotes from Umar and Abu Hazim. What do they say about rulers and desires? How do they support Ibn Asakir's point?
The quotes emphasize that good rulers protect the people from innovations.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why Ibn Asakir includes this discussion in a work defending Ash'ari theology. How does linking doctrinal unity to political stability strengthen his argument?
This shows that theology is not separate from community leadership.
5
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to see if you grasp the main point of the passage.
The answer is found directly in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلماء السنة إذن مجتمعون والأشعريون منهم جماعتهم في علم الأصول موافقون، إلا أن الله جل ثناؤه جعل استقامة أحوالهم باستقامة ولاة هم وسلامة أغراضهم بذب ولاة هم عنهم وبذلك أخبر من جعل الله تعالى الحق على لسانه وقلبه أمير المؤمنين عمر بن الخطاب رضى الله عنه، وذلك فيما أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ أنا أبو عمرو بن السماك نا تنبل بن إسحاق نا أبو نعيم نا مالك بن أنس عن زيد بن أسلم عن أبيه قال [؟] قال عمر رضى الله عنه عند موته: اعلموا أن الناس لن يزالوا بخير ما استقامت لهم ولاة هم وهداتهم، وقال أبو حازم: ما أخبرنا أبو بكر أحمد ابن الحسن أنا حاجب بن أحمدنا محمد بن حماد حدثنا أبو ضمرة أنس ابن عياض، قال سمعت أبا حازم يقول: لا يزال الناس بخير مالم يقع هذه الأهواء في السلطان هم الذين يذبون عن الناس فإذا وقعت فيهم فمن يذب عنهم
Thus, the scholars of the Sunnah are united, and the Ash'aris among them are in agreement in their group concerning the science of principles (usul). However, Allah Almighty made the uprightness of their conditions dependent upon the uprightness of their rulers, and the safety of their objectives upon the protection of their rulers for them. And that is what the one whom Allah made truth upon his tongue and heart, the Commander of the Faithful Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) informed, as reported to us by Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Hafiz... [chain] ... He said: Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said at his death: Know that the people will continue to be in good as long as their rulers and leaders are upright to them. And Abu Hazim said: ... The people will continue to be in good as long as these desires (ahwa') do not fall upon the ruler, for they are the ones who defend the people. When they fall among them, then who will defend them?
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage asserts the unity of Sunni scholars despite their different specializations. Specifically, the Ash'aris within them agree on the science of usul (theological principles). Ibn Asakir then emphasizes that the well-being of the community depends on just rulers who protect the scholars and their objectives. He supports this with quotes from Umar ibn al-Khattab and Abu Hazim, warning that when desires (ahwa', i.e., heretical innovations) influence the rulers, there is no one left to defend the people. This highlights the importance of righteous leadership in preserving orthodox Islam.

Key Terms
علم الأصول
ولاة
أهواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ash'aris are a distinct sect separate from Sunni consensus.
Correction: Ibn Asakir explicitly states that Ash'aris are part of the unified Sunni community and agree on usul.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what ensures the uprightness of the scholars' conditions?
A) Their own efforts.
B) The uprightness of their rulers.
C) The unity of their beliefs.
D) The absence of desires.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir affirms that Sunni scholars, including Ash'aris, are united in usul, and he emphasizes that the well-being of the community depends on righteous rulers who protect them from heretical desires.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the state of your community, do you see a connection between the integrity of your leaders (in any sphere) and the religious commitment of the people? In what specific ways have you experienced or witnessed this dependence?
?
This passage warns that when desires (ahwa') corrupt rulers, there is no one left to defend the people. Think of a modern example where a leader's personal desires have negatively influenced the religious or moral direction of society. How does that make you feel about your own responsibility to seek and support upright leaders?
?
Imagine you are given a position of authority tomorrow. How would you guard yourself against falling into desires? Write one concrete step you will take this week to protect your heart from the influence of corrupt desires, so that you can be a defender of truth for those under your care.

The Persecution of Ash'aris under Vizier al-Kunduri
Ibn Asakir recounts the persecution of Ash'aris under vizier al-Kunduri and its end.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari school was persecuted under the Seljuk vizier al-Kunduri and how the oppression ended with his death.

Core Idea
Political spite, not theology, drove the persecution of Ash'aris.

This lesson recounts a painful chapter in Ash'ari history, when the school was targeted not by the sultan but by his vizier. The story illustrates how theological labels can be weaponized for political ends, and how oppression can end swiftly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the narrative flow. Note the key events and players.
Focus on the sequence: cursing, persecution, exile, and end.
2
Identify the key figures
Identify Sultan Tughril (Hanafi Sunni), vizier al-Kunduri (Mu'tazili Rafidi), and the persecuted scholars: Abu Uthman al-Sabuni, Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri, and Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni.
3
Analyze the cause of persecution
Understand that while the sultan ordered cursing of innovators, the vizier added the Ash'aris out of personal spite (للتسلى والتشفى). This shows political motives behind the theological crackdown.
4
Reflect on the outcome
Note that the oppression ended with the vizier's destruction (death). Ask yourself why this might be significant for understanding how temporary such trials can be.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الحافظ قدس الله روحه وإنما كان انتشار ما ذكره أبو بكر البيهقى رحمه الله من المحنة واستعار ما أشار بإطفائه في رسالته من الفتنة مما تقدم به من سب حزب الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري في دولة السلطان طغرليك ووزارة أبي نصر منصور بن محمد الكندرى وكان السلطان حنيفا سنيا وكان وزيره معتزليا رافضيا فلما أمر السلطان بلعن المبتدعة على المنابر في الجمع قرن الكندرى للتسلى والتشفى اسم الأشعرية بأسماء أرباب البدع وامتحن الأئمة الأماثل وقصد الصدور الأفاضل وعزل أبا عثمان الصابوني عن الخطابة بنيسابور وفوضها إلى بعض الحنفية فأم الجمهور وخرج الأستاذ أبو القاسم والإمام أبو المعالي الجويني رحمة الله عليهما عن البلد وهان عليهما في مخالفته الاغتراب وفراق الوطن والأهل والولد فلم يكن إلا يسيرا حتى تقشعت تلك السحابة وتبدد بهلك الوزير
The Imam al-Hafiz (may Allah sanctify his soul) said: The spread of what Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi mentioned of the trial (mihna) and the borrowing of the tribulation he indicated in his letter to extinguish, was due to the cursing of the party of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari that had preceded in the state of Sultan Tughril Beg and the vizierate of Abu Nasr Mansur ibn Muhammad al-Kunduri. The sultan was a Hanafi Sunni, but his vizier was a Mu'tazili Rafidi. When the sultan ordered the cursing of the innovators (mubtadi'a) on the pulpits during Friday gatherings, al-Kunduri, for amusement and spite, attached the name of the Ash'aris to the names of the people of innovation. He put the noble imams to the test, targeted the distinguished leaders, removed Abu Uthman al-Sabuni from the khutbah in Nishapur, and assigned it to some Hanafi, who led the congregation. The master Abu al-Qasim and the imam Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni (may Allah have mercy on them) left the city, and it became easy for them, in his opposition, to be strangers and to depart from homeland, family, and children. It was not long until that cloud cleared and dispersed with the destruction (death) of the vizier.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage narrates the historical persecution of the Ash'ari school during the reign of Sultan Tughril Beg (Seljuk) and his vizier al-Kunduri. The sultan was a Hanafi Sunni who ordered the cursing of innovators, but the vizier, who was a Mu'tazili and Rafidi (heretic), maliciously included the Ash'aris in the cursing. He persecuted prominent Ash'ari scholars like Abu Uthman al-Sabuni (removed from preaching), and forced Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri and Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni to flee Nishapur. The oppression ended only with the vizier's death. This illustrates the political dimension of theological conflicts and the resilience of the Ash'ari school.

Key Terms
محنة
سب
مبتدعة
معتزلي
رافضي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that the Ash'ari persecution under the Seljuks was a purely religious conflict between Hanafis and Ash'aris.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the sultan (a Hanafi) did not target Ash'aris; it was the vizier's personal sectarianism (Mu'tazili-Rafidi) that caused him to include Ash'aris in the cursing of innovators. The persecution had a strong political and personal dimension.

Checkpoint
Why did al-Kunduri attach the Ash'aris to the cursing of innovators?
A) Because they were heretics.
B) For amusement and spite (للتسلى والتشفى).
C) Because the sultan ordered it.
D) Because they opposed him politically.

Key Takeaway
The persecution of Ash'aris under al-Kunduri was driven by the vizier's sectarian spite and ended with his death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever twisted a legitimate command or rule to settle a personal grudge, like al-Kunduri twisted the sultan's order? What does that reveal about your heart? How can you repent and change that pattern today?
?
When you see others being persecuted or marginalized, do you remain silent like the sultan (who allowed his vizier to act) or do you intervene? What is one step you can take this week to stand up for someone being treated unjustly?
?
The Ash'ari scholars left their homes, families, and positions rather than compromise. Is there any worldly comfort you would be unwilling to leave behind for the sake of truth? Ask Allah to give you that level of sincerity.

The Ash'ari Persecution and Restoration under the Seljuks
Ibn 'Asakir narrates the persecution of Ash'aris and its reversal by Nizam al-Mulk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical trial (mihna) faced by the Ash'ari school under the Seljuk vizier al-Kunduri and how it was reversed by Nizam al-Mulk, and the lesson that divine justice ultimately prevails.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari persecution was a vizier's vendetta; divine justice restored them through Nizam al-Mulk.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari narrates a dramatic episode in Islamic history: the brief but intense persecution of the Ash'ari school under the Seljuk vizier al-Kunduri, and its reversal under the famous vizier Nizam al-Mulk. It highlights how the Ash'aris, though initially cursed and exiled, were eventually vindicated, drawing a parallel to the cursing of Ali ibn Abi Talib. This historical account reinforces the Sunni doctrine that the Ash'ari school is part of the orthodox tradition, despite temporary opposition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the persecutor
Learn about Vizier al-Kunduri, his sectarian motives, and his actions against the Ash'ari scholars.
The text notes he was Mu'tazili and Rafidi, and acted out of amusement and vengeance.
2
Describe the persecution
List the specific events: cursing on pulpits, removal of Abu Uthman al-Sabuni, exile of al-Qushayri and al-Juwayni.
Observe how the scholars chose exile rather than submission.
3
Note the reversal
See how the death of al-Kunduri and Sultan Tughril, and the rise of Alp Arslan and Nizam al-Mulk, reversed the situation.
Nizam al-Mulk restored honor to the Ash'aris, building schools and mosques.
4
Reflect on the moral
Consider Ibn 'Asakir's parallel to Ali (ra) and al-Qushayri's poem – iniquity is temporary, divine justice is enduring.
The lesson is that truth cannot be permanently suppressed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الحافظ قدس الله روحه وإنما كان انتشار ما ذكره أبو بكر البيهقى رحمه الله من المحنة واستعار ما أشار باطفائه في رسالته من الفتنة مما تقدم به من سب حزب الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري في دولة السلطان طغرليك ووزارة أبي نصر منصور بن محمد الكندرى وكان السلطان حنيفا سنيا وكان وزيره معتزلیا رافضيا فلما أمر السلطان بلعن المبتدعة على المنابر في الجمع قرن الكندرى للتسلى والتشفى اسم الأشعرية بأسماء أرباب البدع وامتحن الأئمة الاماثل وقصد الصدور الافاضل وعزل أبا عثمان الصابوني عن الخطابة بنيسابور وفوضها إلى بعض الحنفية فأم الجمهور وخرج الأستاذ أبو القسم والإمام أبو المعالي الجويني رحمة الله عليهما عن البلد وهان عليهما في مخالفته الاغتراب وفراق الوطن والأهل والولد فلم يكن الا يسيرا حتى تقشعت تلك السحابة وتبدد بهلك الوزير شمل تلك العصابة ومات ذلك السلطان وولى ابنه آلب ارسلان و استوزر الوزير الكامل والصدر العالم العادل ابا على الحسن بن على بن اسحق فأعز أهل السنة وقمع أهل النفاق وأمر باسقاط ذكرهم من السب وافراد من عاداهم باللعن والثلب واسترجع من خرج منهم إلى وطنه واستقدمه مكرما بعد بعده وظعنه وبنى لهم المساجد والمدارس وعقد لهم الحلق والمجالس وبنى لهم الجامع المنيعى فى أيام ولد ذلك السلطان، وكان ذلك تداركا لما سلف في حقهم من الامتحان، فاستقام في وزارته الدين بعد اعوجاجه وصفا عيش أهل السنة بعد تكدره وامتزاجه واستقر الأمر بيمن نقيبته على ذلك إلى هذا الوقت ونظر أرباب البدع بعين الاحتقار والمقت، ولم يضر جمع الفرقة المنصورة ما فرط في حقهم في المدة اليسيرة ممن قصدهم بالمساءة ورماهم بالشناعة لما ظهر فيهم اللعن اذ كانوا براء عند العقلاء وأهل العلم من الابتداع والذم والطعن ولهم في أمير المؤمنين على بن أبى طالب رضی الله عنه أسوة حسنة، فقد كان يسب على المنابر في الدولة الأموية نحوا من ثمانين سنة فما ضر ذلك عليا رضوان الله عليه ولا التحق به ما نسب اليه وقتل الوزير شر قتلة بعد ما مثل به كل مثلة، فقال الاستاذ أبو القسم القشيري رضي الله عنه فيه : عميد الملك ساعدك الليالي على ما شئت في درك المعالي فلم يك منك شيء غير أمر بلعن المسلمين على التوالي فقابلك البلاء بما تلاقى فذق ما تستحق من الوبال أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبدالله محمد بن الفضل الفقيه أخبرنا الأستاذ أبو القسم القشيرى رضى الله عنه قال : الحمد لله المجمل في بلائه المجزل في عطائه العدل في قضائه، المكرم لأوليائه، المنتقم من اعدائه الناصر لدينه بايضاح الحق وتبيينه المبيد للإفك وأهله المجتث للباطل من أصله، فاضح البدع بلسان العلماء وكاشف الشبه ببيان الحكماء وممهل الغواة حينا غير مهملهم، ومجازى كل غدا على مقتضى عملهم، نحمده على ما عرفنا من توحيده ونستوفقه على ما كلفنا من رعاية حدوده، ونستعصمه من الخطأ والخطل والزيغ والزلل فى القول والعمل ونسأله أن يصلى على سيدنا
The Imam, the Hafiz, may Allah sanctify his soul, said: The spread of what Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned of the trial, and the fanning of the flame of the fitna that he indicated to extinguish in his letter, was due to the cursing of the party of Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari that had preceded in the state of Sultan Tughril Beg and the vizierate of Abu Nasr Mansur ibn Muhammad al-Kunduri. The sultan was Hanafi and Sunni, and his vizier was Mu'tazili and Rafidi. When the sultan ordered the cursing of innovators on the pulpits on Fridays, al-Kunduri, for amusement and vengeance, included the name of the Ash'aris with the names of the people of innovation. He tested the eminent imams and targeted the virtuous leaders. He removed Abu Uthman al-Sabuni from the khutbah in Nishapur and entrusted it to some Hanafi, who led the congregation. The master Abu al-Qasim and the imam Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni, may Allah have mercy on them, left the city, and it became easy for them in opposing him to be estranged and to leave home, family, and child. It was not long before that cloud dispersed and the group was scattered with the death of the vizier. The sultan died and his son Alp Arslan succeeded. He appointed as vizier the perfect vizier and the just, learned leader Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ishaq. He strengthened the people of the Sunnah and suppressed the people of hypocrisy. He ordered the removal of their mention from cursing and singled out those who opposed them for curse and rebuke. He brought back those of them who had left their homeland, and brought them back honored after their distance and travel. He built for them mosques and schools, and established for them circles and assemblies, and built for them the Mani'i mosque in the days of the son of that sultan. That was a reparation for what had preceded of trial against them. So the religion became upright in his vizierate after its crookedness, and the life of the people of the Sunnah became clear after its turbidity and mixture. The affair became established by the blessing of his leadership until this time. The people of innovation looked with the eye of contempt and hatred. It did not harm the gathered victorious sect what was excessive against them in the short period from those who intended them with harm and accused them of disgrace because of the cursing that appeared against them, since they were innocent in the eyes of the rational and the people of knowledge of innovation, blame, and slander. They have in the Commander of the Faithful, Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, a good example. He was cursed on the pulpits during the Umayyad state for about eighty years, and that did not harm Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, nor did what was attributed to him stick. The vizier was killed the worst killing after being mutilated in every way. Then the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri, may Allah be pleased with him, said concerning him: 'O pillar of the kingdom, the nights aided you in attaining high ranks as you wished. But nothing came from you except an order to curse Muslims continuously. So the affliction met you with what you met, so taste what you deserve of calamity.' The sheikh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Faqih informed us that the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri, may Allah be pleased with him, said: Praise be to Allah, the Benevolent in His trial, the Munificent in His giving, the Just in His decree, the One Who honors His friends, the Avenger from His enemies, the Helper of His religion by clarifying the truth and explaining it, the Destroyer of falsehood and its people, the Uprooter of falsehood from its root, the Exposer of innovations by the tongue of the scholars, the Remover of doubts by the explanation of the wise, the One Who gives respite to the misguided for a time but does not neglect them, the One Who rewards everyone tomorrow according to their deeds. We praise Him for what He has taught us of His tawheed, and we seek His success in what He has charged us with of observing His limits. We seek His protection from error, foolishness, deviation, and stumbling in speech and deed. And we ask Him to pray upon our master...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative by Ibn 'Asakir detailing the persecution of the Ash'ari school under the Seljuk sultan Tughril Beg and his vizier al-Kunduri, and its subsequent reversal under Sultan Alp Arslan and the vizier Nizam al-Mulk. The passage begins by explaining that the spread of the fitna described earlier was caused by the cursing of the party of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari that had occurred during the reign of Sultan Tughril Beg and the vizierate of Abu Nasr al-Kunduri. The sultan was a Hanafi Sunni, but his vizier was a Mu'tazili Rafidi. When the sultan ordered the cursing of innovators from the pulpits, the vizier al-Kunduri, for amusement and vengeance, included the Ash'aris among the innovators. He persecuted the leading imams and removed Abu Uthman al-Sabuni from the khutbah in Nishapur, appointing a Hanafi in his place. This led to the departure of two prominent scholars, Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri and Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni, from the city, who accepted estrangement and separation from family for the sake of opposing the vizier. However, the situation soon turned: the cloud of oppression dispersed with the death of the vizier. Then Sultan Tughril died, and his son Alp Arslan took over. He appointed the just vizier Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ishaq (Nizam al-Mulk), who revived the Sunnah, suppressed hypocrisy, removed the Ash'aris from the cursing, and instead cursed their opponents. He restored the exiled scholars, built mosques and schools for them, and established their gatherings. This was a reparation for the earlier trial. The religion became upright again. Ibn 'Asakir then notes that the harm done to the Ash'aris in that short period did not ultimately hurt them, because they were innocent in the eyes of the wise. He draws a parallel to Ali ibn Abi Talib, who was cursed for eighty years under the Umayyads but remained unharmed. Finally, the vizier al-Kunduri was killed in the worst manner. At this point, the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri composed a poem addressing the vizier: 'O pillar of the kingdom, the nights aided you in attaining high ranks, but nothing came from you except an order to curse Muslims continuously. So the affliction met you with what you met, so taste what you deserve of calamity.' The passage ends with a sermon by al-Qushayri praising Allah for His attributes—His benevolence in trial, munificence, justice, honor of friends, vengeance from enemies, support of truth, destruction of falsehood, exposure of innovations by scholars, removal of doubts, giving respite to the misguided, and rewarding each according to deeds. He then praises Allah for teaching tawheed and seeks success in fulfilling His commands, protection from error, and sends blessings on the Prophet (the sentence is cut off at the end of the page).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash'ari persecution was ordered by the caliph or sultan as a general policy, but it was actually the vizier al-Kunduri's personal agenda driven by his Mu'tazili and Rafidi leanings.
Correction: The text explicitly states that the sultan ordered cursing of innovators, but the vizier, on his own initiative, included the Ash'aris out of amusement and vengeance.

Checkpoint
Why did the vizier al-Kunduri include the Ash'aris in the curse on the pulpits?
A) He was ordered by the sultan to curse all innovators.
B) He was a Mu'tazili Rafidi who sought amusement and vengeance against them.
C) He wanted to please the Hanafis.
D) He was following the practice of the Umayyads.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school, though persecuted briefly, was vindicated by divine justice and the support of righteous leaders like Nizam al-Mulk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see injustice against a group of Muslims today, do you trust that Allah will eventually bring justice, even if it takes years? What is one step you can take to actively support the truth without resorting to the same methods of your oppressors?
?
The vizier al-Kunduri used his power to curse innocent people for personal vengeance. Examine your own life: is there any position or influence you have—even within your family or community—that you might be tempted to misuse to harm others? How will you safeguard yourself from that sin starting today?
?
Imagine you were one of the scholars who had to leave home, family, and children for the sake of truth. Would you be willing to do the same if your faith required it? If not, what does that reveal about your attachment to this world?

Al-Qabisi's Defense of al-Ash'ari
Al-Qabisi defends al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy and explains his role in clarifying the Sunna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Qabisi's defense of al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy and how he argued that al-Ash'ari's kalam was meant to clarify and defend the Sunna.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's kalam clarified the Sunna; his death proved his orthodoxy.

Al-Qabisi, a prominent Maliki scholar, wrote a treatise defending Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari against accusations of innovation. In this passage, he explains that al-Ash'ari's engagement with kalam was solely to clarify and confirm the Sunna and repel doubts. He also addresses a claim that tawhid is only completed by al-Ash'ari's doctrine, refuting it by pointing to the consensus of Sunni scholars honoring him at his death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from praising earlier scholars to the core defense of al-Ash'ari.
The passage has OCR issues; some words may need correction (e.g., 'قبال' likely 'قال').
2
Identify al-Qabisi's main claim about al-Ash'ari's purpose
Find where al-Qabisi states why al-Ash'ari engaged in kalam. Look for the phrase 'ايضاح السنن والتثبيت عليها ودفع الشبه عنها'.
This is the central thesis: kalam to clarify the Sunna.
3
Analyze the refutation of the tawhid objection
Someone claimed that tawhid is only completed by al-Ash'ari's doctrine. Al-Qabisi refutes this by pointing out the reaction to al-Ash'ari's death: Sunnis wept, heretics rejoiced. Understand why this proves his orthodoxy.
The idea: if al-Ash'ari had deviated, Sunnis would not have mourned him.
4
Reflect on the significance of the passage
Ask yourself: How does this defense establish al-Ash'ari's place within Sunni orthodoxy? What does it tell us about the early perception of kalam?
This connects to the broader theme of defending kalam as a tool for preserving the Sunna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الشيوخ المتأخرين المشاهير أبو محمد بن أبي زيد وشهرته تغنى عن ذكر فضله اجتمع فيه العقل والدين والعلم والورع ، وكان يلقب بمالك الصغير وخاطبه من بغداد رجل معتزلی يرغبه في مذهب الاعتزال ويقول له انه مذهب مالك وأصحابه فجاوبه بجواب من وقف عليه علم انه كان نهاية في علم الأصول رضى الله وبعده ومعه الشيخ الفاضل الكامل أبو الحسن القابسي متأخبر في زمانه متقدم فى شأنه جمع العلم والعمل والرواية والدراية من ذوى الاجتهاد في العباد والزهاد، مجاب الدعوة له مناقب يضيق عنها هذا الكتاب كان عالما بالأصول والفروع والحديث وغير ذلك من الرقائق ودقيق الورع وله رسالة في أبي الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه احسن الثناء عليه وذكر فضله وامامته، ثم ذكر الكلاعي جماعة من افاضل هذا العلم بالمغرب تركت ذكرهم تجنبا للاطالة خوفا من السآمة والملالة . قبال الشيخ الامام الحافظ رضى الله عنه قرأت بخط بعض أهل العلم بالفقه والحديث من أهل الاندلس ممن أثق به فيما يحكيه وأصدقه فيما يرويه في جواب سؤال سئل عنه أبو الحسن على الفقيه القيرواني المعروف بابن القابسي وهو من كبار أئمة المالكية بالمغرب، سأله عنه بعض أهل تونس من بلاد المغرب فكان في جوابه له أن قال واعلموا أن أبا الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه لم يأت من هذا الأمر يعنى الكلام إلا ما أراد به الله ايضاح السنن والتثبيت عليها ودفع الشبه عنها فهمه من فهمه بفضل عليه وخفى عمن خفى بقسم الله له وما أبو الحسن الأشعري إلا واحد من جملة القائمين بنصر الحق ما سمعنا من أهل الانصاف من يؤخره عن رتبته ذلك ولا من يؤثر عليه في عصره غيره ومن بعده من أهل الحق سلكوا سبيله في القيام بأمر الله عز وجل والذب عن دينه حسب اجتهادهم قال واما قولكم وان كان التوحيد لايتم إلا بمقالة الأشعرى فهذا يدل على انكم . فهمتم ان الأشعرى قال في التوحيد قولا خرج به عن أهل الحق، فإن كان قد نسب هذا المعنى عندكم إلى الأشعرى فقد أبطل من قال ذلك عليه، لقدمات الأشعرى رضى الله عنه يوم مات وأهل السنة باكون عليه، وأهل البدع مستريحون منه ، فما عرفه، من وصفه بغير هذا قال رضى الله
And among the later notable scholars is Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Zayd, whose fame suffices from mentioning his virtue. He combined intellect, religion, knowledge, and piety. He was nicknamed 'the young Malik'. A Mu'tazilite man from Baghdad corresponded with him, enticing him to the Mu'tazilite school, saying it was the school of Malik and his companions. He replied with a response that whoever sees it knows he was the ultimate in the science of principles (usul). May Allah be pleased with him. After him and with him is the virtuous, perfect sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Qabisi, later in his time, advanced in his status. He combined knowledge, action, transmission, and insight from those of ijtihad in worship and asceticism. His supplication was answered; he had merits that this book cannot contain. He was knowledgeable in principles, branches, hadith, and other spiritual subtleties and delicate piety. He wrote a treatise on Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, praising him and mentioning his virtue and imamate. Then al-Kala'i mentioned a group of the excellent ones of this knowledge in the Maghreb, but I left their mention to avoid length, fearing boredom and weariness. The sheikh, the imam, the hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: I read in the handwriting of some people of knowledge in fiqh and hadith from the people of Andalusia, whom I trust in what he narrates and believe him in what he relates, in response to a question asked about Abu al-Hasan 'Ali al-Faqih al-Qayrawani, known as Ibn al-Qabisi, who is among the great Maliki imams in the Maghreb. Some people from Tunis in the Maghreb asked him, and in his response he said: 'Know that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, only came with this matter – meaning kalam – with what Allah intended: clarification of the Sunna, confirmation upon it, and repelling doubts from it. He who understood it understood it by virtue from Allah, and it was hidden from whoever it was hidden by Allah's decree. Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is only one of those who stood for supporting the truth. We have not heard from the people of fairness anyone who would downgrade him from his rank, nor anyone who would prefer another over him in his time. And after him, the people of truth followed his path in standing for the command of Allah Almighty and defending His religion according to their ijtihad.' He said: 'As for your statement, "Tawhid is only completed by the doctrine of al-Ash'ari," this indicates that you understood that al-Ash'ari said something in tawhid that deviated from the people of truth. If this meaning is attributed to al-Ash'ari according to you, then whoever said that about him has nullified it, because when al-Ash'ari died, may Allah be pleased with him, on the day he died, the People of the Sunna wept over him, and the people of innovation were relieved from him. So whoever describes him with other than this does not know him.' He said, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari written by al-Qabisi. It begins with praising two later scholars: Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Zayd (known as Malik al-Saghir) and Abu al-Hasan al-Qabisi himself. Then it transitions into a response to a question about al-Ash'ari. The response clarifies that al-Ash'ari only used kalam to clarify and defend the Sunna, not to innovate. It asserts that al-Ash'ari is one of the supporters of truth, and the people of fairness respect him. The passage addresses an objection that some claim tawhid is only completed by al-Ash'ari's doctrine, which might imply that al-Ash'ari deviated. Al-Qabisi refutes this by pointing out that at al-Ash'ari's death, the Sunnis wept and the heretics rejoiced, proving his orthodoxy. Thus, anyone who describes him otherwise does not truly know him.

أبو الحسن الأشعرى
توحيد
كلام
سنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Ash'ari introduced a new doctrine or deviated from the Sunnah.
Correction: Al-Qabisi argues that al-Ash'ari only clarified the Sunna and repelled doubts, and his death reveals that Sunnis mourned him while heretics were relieved, confirming his orthodoxy.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qabisi, what was the purpose of al-Ash'ari's work in kalam?
A) To create a new sect
B) To clarify the Sunna and repel doubts
C) To oppose the Maliki school
D) To gain fame

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's kalam served to clarify the Sunna, and his death revealed his true status among Sunnis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine your own life: if you were to die today, would the people of truth weep for you and the people of falsehood rejoice? What does that reveal about your true allegiance?
?
Do you use your knowledge to clarify the truth and defend the Sunna, or do you sometimes promote your own opinions? Ask yourself honestly: what is the ultimate goal of your learning?
?
Al-Ash'ari's death exposed his inner reality. How would your death expose yours? What changes must you make now to ensure you are with the people of truth?

Ibn Abi Zayd's Defense of al-Ash'ari
Ibn Abi Zayd writes a letter refuting a Mu'tazili's accusations against al-Ash'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a leading Maliki scholar defended al-Ash'ari against Mu'tazili accusations by highlighting his role in refuting innovation and adhering to the sunan.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari is defended as a refuter of innovators and a follower of the sunan.

In this passage, we read an excerpt from a letter by the famous Maliki jurist Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani. He responds to a Mu'tazili critic who had attacked Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Ibn Abi Zayd's brief but powerful defense presents al-Ash'ari as a staunch opponent of heresy and a faithful adherent to the prophetic traditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage slowly, then read the English translation. Notice the structure: it begins with the source of the letter, then states the accusation, then gives the defense.
The passage is from a manuscript copy by 'Ali ibn Baqa'.
2
Identify the three groups al-Ash'ari refutes
Ibn Abi Zayd lists three groups: ahl al-bida' (people of innovation), al-Qadariyya, and al-Jahmiyya. Ask yourself what these groups represent in early Islamic theology.
The Mu'tazila were often associated with Qadariyya and Jahmiyya by their opponents.
3
Understand the function of the letter
This letter is a refutation (jawaab) to a Mu'tazili. Ibn Abi Zayd does not argue at length; instead he states a well-known fact about al-Ash'ari's reputation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقرأت بخط على بن بقاء المصرى الوراق المحدث في رسالة كتب بها أبو محمد عبدالله بن أبي زيد القيرواني المالكي (۱) جوابا لعلی بن احمد بن اسمعيل البغدادى المعتزلى حين ذكر ابا الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه ونسبه إلى ما هو برىء منه مما جرت عادة المعتزلة باستعمال مثله في حقه فقال ابن أبي زيد في حق أبى الحسن هو رجل مشهور انه يرد على أهل البدع وعلى القدرية والجهمية متمسك بالسنن
And I read in the handwriting of 'Ali ibn Baqa' al-Misri al-Warraq al-Muhaddith in a letter that was written by Abu Muhammad 'Abdullah ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani al-Maliki (1) as a reply to 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Isma'il al-Baghdadi al-Mu'tazili, when he mentioned Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, and attributed to him what he is innocent of, of the sort that the Mu'tazila customarily use against him. So Ibn Abi Zayd said about Abu al-Hasan: 'He is a well-known man who refutes the people of innovation, the Qadariyya, and the Jahmiyya, adhering to the sunan.'
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an excerpt from a letter written by Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani in response to a Mu'tazili critic. It first establishes the source: a manuscript by 'Ali ibn Baqa' al-Misri. The letter was composed to refute accusations against al-Ash'ari that the Mu'tazila habitually made. Ibn Abi Zayd's defense is succinct: al-Ash'ari is famous for refuting the people of innovation (ahl al-bida'), the Qadariyya, and the Jahmiyya, and he adheres firmly to the sunan. This directly counters the Mu'tazili claim by presenting al-Ash'ari as a defender of orthodoxy.

Key Terms
ابن أبي زيد
المعتزلة
القدرية
الجهمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari was a Mu'tazili or an innovator.
Correction: The passage shows that Ibn Abi Zayd presents al-Ash'ari as someone who refutes innovators (ahl al-bida') and adheres to the sunan, indicating his orthodox stance.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abi Zayd, what does al-Ash'ari do concerning people of innovation?
A) He avoids them
B) He refutes them
C) He agrees with them
D) He ignores them

Key Takeaway
Ibn Abi Zayd defends al-Ash'ari by affirming his role as a refuter of innovators and a follower of the sunan, countering Mu'tazili accusations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone attacking a scholar you respect, do you respond with accurate knowledge like Ibn Abi Zayd, or with emotion and ignorance? What would it take for you to be able to defend truth with clear evidence?
?
Ibn Abi Zayd wrote a letter to correct a false accusation. Have you ever been the one spreading false information about someone—even unintentionally? What will you do differently now to ensure you speak only the truth?
?
Al-Ash'ari is described as 'adhering to the sunan.' How tightly are you clinging to the sunnah in your daily life? Identify one specific area where you are letting go and commit to holding on again.

Al-Ash'ari's Fiqh Mastery
A story showing al-Ash'ari's mastery of fiqh by quoting hadith on the Fatiha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's response to a fiqh question demonstrated his mastery of hadith and silenced a critic.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari was not only a theologian; he was also a master of hadith and fiqh.

This short anecdote reveals a lesser-known side of al-Ash'ari: his deep knowledge of prophetic hadith. After dominating a theological debate, he was challenged on a practical fiqh issue. His response, citing two chains of narration for the same ruling, left his questioner speechless.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Understand the context: al-Ash'ari had silenced the Mu'tazila in debate. Then a questioner tests him on a fiqh issue, expecting him to fail.
Notice the challenge: 'We know your deep knowledge in kalam, but I ask you about an apparent issue in fiqh.'
2
Note al-Ash'ari's method
Al-Ash'ari does not give a personal opinion. Instead, he cites two hadiths with full chains of narration, showing his expertise in hadith.
He quotes from Zakariyya al-Saji, then from Bandar — both chains lead to the Prophet.
3
Reflect on the lesson
This story shows that al-Ash'ari was not only a mutakallim but also a scholar of hadith and fiqh. It addresses the misconception that he only excelled in theology.
The questioner fell silent, confirming al-Ash'ari's point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدثنى الثقة من أصحابنا قال نا القاضي أبو اسحق ابراهيم بن على بن الحسين الشيباني الطبري، ثم المكي من لفظه ببغداد وقد لقيت انا القاضى ابا اسحق ببغداد وصاحبته في طريق مكة ولم أسمع منه شيئا قال نا الحافظ أبو نعيم منه شيئا قال نا الحافظ أبو نعيم عبيد الله بن الحسن ابن احمد بن الحسن بأصبهان نا أبو ابراهيم اسعد بن مسعـود الـعـتـبـي بنيسابور، أخبرنا الأستاذ الامام أبو منصور عبد القاهر بن طاهر البغدادي قال سمعت عبد الله بن محمد بن طاهر الصوفى يقول رأيت أبا الحسن الله عنه في مسجد البصرة وقد أبهت المعتزلة في المناظرة الأشعرى رضى الله فقال له بعض الحاضرين قد عرفنا تبحرك في علم الكلام وانا اسألك عن مسألة ظاهرة فى الفقه فقال سل عما شئت فقال له ماتقول في الصلاة بغير فاتحة الكتاب فقال نا زكريا بن يحيى الساجي نا عبد الجبار نا سفیان حدثني الزهري عن محمود بن الربيع عن عبادة بن الصامت عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ( لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب ) (۲) قال وحدثنا زكريا نا بندار نا یحیی بن سعید عن جعفر بن ميمون حدثني أبو عثمن عن أبى هريرة رضى الله عنه قال امرنی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان انادى بالمدينة انه لا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب قال فسكت السائل ولم يقل شيئا .
A trusted companion of ours narrated to me, saying: al-Qadi Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn al-Shaybani al-Tabari, then al-Makki, narrated to us from his dictation in Baghdad — and I met al-Qadi Abu Ishaq in Baghdad and accompanied him on the road to Mecca but did not hear anything from him — he said: al-Hafiz Abu Nu'aym narrated to us … he said: al-Hafiz Abu Nu'aym 'Ubaydullah ibn al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan in Isfahan narrated to us: Abu Ibrahim As'ad ibn Mas'ud al-'Utbi in Nishapur narrated to us: the teacher, the imam Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Qahir ibn Tahir al-Baghdadi informed us, saying: I heard 'Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Tahir al-Sufi say: I saw Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, in the mosque of Basra, and he had silenced the Mu'tazila in debate. So one of those present said to him: 'We know your deep knowledge in kalam, but I ask you about an apparent issue in fiqh.' He said: 'Ask whatever you wish.' He said: 'What do you say about prayer without the Fatiha?' He said: 'Zakariyya ibn Yahya al-Saji narrated to us, 'Abd al-Jabbar narrated to us, Sufyan narrated to me, al-Zuhri narrated to me, from Mahmud ibn al-Rabi', from 'Ubada ibn al-Samit, from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: "No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha." ' He said: 'And Zakariyya narrated to us: Bandar narrated to us, Yahya ibn Sa'id narrated to us, from Ja'far ibn Maimun, Abu 'Uthman narrated to me, from Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, ordered me to announce in Medina that there is no prayer except with the Fatiha.' He said: The questioner fell silent and did not say anything.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an anecdote transmitted through a chain of narrators, illustrating al-Ash'ari's competence in fiqh despite his fame in kalam. After al-Ash'ari had silenced the Mu'tazila in a debate, a skeptic challenged him on a fiqh issue, expecting him to falter. Al-Ash'ari responded by reciting two hadith chains proving the necessity of reciting the Fatiha in prayer. The first hadith is from 'Ubada ibn al-Samit: 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha.' The second is from Abu Hurayra: the Prophet ordered him to announce in Medina that there is no prayer except with the Fatiha. The questioner fell silent, confirming al-Ash'ari's point. This story demonstrates that al-Ash'ari was not only a mutakallim but also a scholar of hadith and fiqh.

Key Terms
فاتحة الكتاب
المناظرة
علم الكلام
علم الفقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari was only a theologian and not versed in hadith or fiqh.
Correction: This anecdote shows he was also a master of fiqh, able to cite hadith from memory with full chains.

Checkpoint
What did al-Ash'ari quote to answer the question about prayer?
A) A Qur'anic verse
B) A hadith from the Prophet
C) An opinion of a scholar
D) A logical proof

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's response shows that a true scholar of kalam is also grounded in the primary sources of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are challenged on a point of deen, do you instinctively reach for rational arguments or do you first recall the Quran and hadith? What does this story teach you about the importance of being grounded in the primary sources?
?
Al-Ash'ari, a master of kalam, did not hesitate to answer a fiqh question by citing hadith. Where in your own life do you need to humble yourself and admit that you must learn from areas you may have overlooked?
?
If someone were to ask you about a ruling you are unsure of, would you be quick to fall silent like the challenger or would you strive to find the evidence? How can you ensure that your knowledge is built on the foundation of revelation?

The Mu'tazila Method: Tafsir by Personal Opinion
Ibn Asakir condemns Mu'tazila tafsir as opinion-based and lists its early proponents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's critique that Mu'tazila tafsir relied on personal opinion rather than transmitted authority from the Salaf.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila tafsir is based on whims, not transmission.

Ibn Asakir begins by praising the Quran's miraculous nature and its clear distinction between truth and falsehood. Then he sharply condemns the Mu'tazila for interpreting the Quran according to their own desires, without relying on prophetic tradition or the understanding of the early Muslims. This passage establishes the Sunni critique of rationalist tafsir.

Guided Path
1
Read the praise of the Quran
Notice how Ibn Asakir describes the Quran as a clear proof, containing abrogation, Meccan/Medinan, etc. This sets the standard against which Mu'tazila tafsir will be judged.
The praise also emphasizes the Quran's miraculous nature.
2
Identify the shift to critique
The phrase 'اما بعد' marks a transition. Now Ibn Asakir attacks those who interpret the Quran by their own opinions.
3
Examine the list of Mu'tazila figures
Ibn Asakir names eight early Mu'tazila scholars as the sources of this corrupted tafsir. Each name represents a chain of misguidance.
The list includes Abu Hudhayl, al-Nazzam, al-Fuwati, al-Jubba'i, al-Ashajj, Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, al-Askafi, and al-Farawi.
4
Understand why they are 'leaders of misguidance'
Ibn Asakir calls them 'قادة الضلال' and says their followers blindly imitate them, making them the pillars of their religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أهل الافك والبهتان ونقض ما حرفه الجبائى والبلخى في تأليفهما قال في أوله : الحمد لله الحميد المجيد المبدىء المعيد الفعال لما يريد الذي افتتح بحمده ،كتابه، وأوضح فيه برهانه وبين فيه حلاله وحرامه وفرق بين الحق والباطل، والعالم والجاهل، وأنزله محكما ومتشابها وناسخا ومنسوخا، ومكيا ومدنيا وخاصا وعاما، ومثلا مضروبا اخبر فيه عن أخبار الأولين وأقاصيص المتقدمين ورغب فيه في الطاعات ورهب فيه وزجر عن الزلات والتبعات وخطوات الشيطان والضلالات ووعد فيه بالثواب لمن عمل بطاعته ليوم المآب وتوعد فيه من كفر به وجانب الصواب ولم يعمل بالطاعة ليوم الحشر والحساب جعله موعظة للمؤمنين وعبرة للغابرين وحجة على العالمين لئلا يقولوا ربنا لولا أرسلت إلينا رسولا فنتبع آياتك ونكون من المؤمنين جمع فيه علم الأولين والآخرين، وأكمل فيه الفرائض والدين فهو صراط الله المستبين وحبله المتين من تمسك به نجا ومن جانبه ضل وغوی وفي الجهل تردى وجعله قرآنا عربيا غير ذى عوج بلسان العرب الأميين الذين لم يأتهم رسول قبله من عند رب العالمين بكتاب يتلوه بلسانهم من عند فاطر السموات والأرضين وقطع به عذر المخالفين لنبوة سيد الرسلين إذ جعله معجزا يعجزون عن الآتيان بمثله وهم أرباب اللسان والنهاية في البيان بين لهم فيه مايأتون ومايتقون وما يحلون وما يحرمون وأوضح لهم فيه سبل الرشاد والهدى والسداد وماصنعه بالأولين الذين كانوا لدينه مخالفين وعنه منحرفين وما ينزله من النقمات بالكافرين ان اقاموا على الكفر وكانوا به متمسكين ليهلك هلك من عن بينة ويحيا من حي عن بينة وان الله السميع عليم اما بعد فإن أهل الزيغ والتضليل تأولوا القرآن على آرائهم وفسروه على أهوائهم تفسيرا لم ينزل الله به سلطانا، ولا أوضح به برهانا ولا رووه عن رسول رب العالمين ولا عن أهل بيته الطيبين ولا عن السلف المتقدمين من أصحابه والتابعين، افتراء على الله قد ضلوا وما كانوا مهتدين، وإنما اخذوا تفسيرهم عن أبي الهذيل بياع العلف ومتبعية، وعن إبراهيم نظام الخرز ومقلديه، وعن الفوطى وناصريه وعن المنسوب إلى قرية جبى ومنتحليه وعن الأشج جعفر بن حرب ومجتبيه وعن جعفر بن مبشر القصبى ومتعصبيه وعن الأسكافى الجاهل ومعظميه، وعن الفروى المنسوب إلى مدينة بلخ وذويه فإنهم قادة الضلال من المعتزلة الجهال، الذين قلدوهم دينهم وجعلوهم معولهم، الذى عليه يعولون وركنهم الذى إليه يستندون ورأيت الجبائى ألف في تفسير القرآن كتابا أوله على خلاف ما أنزل الله عز وجل وعلى لغة أهل قريته المعروفة بجبى وليس من أهل اللسان الذي نزل به القرآن وماروى فى كتابه حرفا واحدا عن أحد من المفسرين وإنما اعتمد على ماوسوس به صدره وشيطانه ولولا انه استغوى بكتابه كثيرا من العوام واستنزل به عن الحق كثيرا من الطغام، لم يكن لتشاغلی به وجه . قال الامام الحافظ أبو القسم رضى الله عنه ثم ذكر بعض المواضع التي اخطأ فيها الجبائى فى تفسيره، وبين ما اخطأ فيه من تأويل القرآن بعون الله له وتيسيره وكل ذلك مما يدل على نبله وكثرة علمه وظهور فضله، فجزاه الله على جهاده في دينه بلسانه الحسنى وأحله باحسانه في مستقر جنانه المحل الأسنى .
The people of falsehood and slander and the refutation of what al-Jubba'i and al-Balkhi distorted in their books. He said in its beginning: Praise be to Allah, the Praiseworthy, the Glorious, the Beginner, the Restorer, the Doer of whatever He wills, who opened His book with His praise, and clarified in it His proof, and explained in it His lawful and His unlawful, and distinguished between truth and falsehood, and the knowledgeable and the ignorant, and sent it down as definitive and ambiguous, abrogating and abrogated, Meccan and Medinan, specific and general, and a parable set forth. He informed in it of the news of the ancients and the stories of the predecessors, and encouraged in it obedience, and warned and forbade in it from slips, transgressions, the steps of Satan, and misguidances. And He promised in it reward for those who act in obedience to Him for the Day of Return, and threatened in it those who disbelieve in it and avoid the truth and do not act obediently for the Day of Gathering and Reckoning. He made it an admonition for the believers, a lesson for those who come after, and a proof against the worlds, lest they say, 'Our Lord, why did You not send us a messenger so that we might follow Your verses and be among the believers?' He gathered in it the knowledge of the first and the last, and perfected in it the obligations and the religion. So it is the clear path of Allah and His strong rope. Whoever holds fast to it is saved, and whoever opposes it goes astray and errs and falls into ignorance. And He made it an Arabic Quran, without crookedness, in the tongue of the unlettered Arabs, to whom no messenger before him came from the Lord of the worlds with a book to recite to them in their tongue from the Originator of the heavens and the earths. And He cut off the excuse of the opponents of the prophethood of the Master of the Messengers, since He made it a miracle that they are incapable of producing the like of it, while they are masters of speech and utmost in eloquence. He made clear to them what they should do, what they should avoid, what is lawful, what is unlawful, and He clarified for them the paths of righteousness, guidance, and rectitude, and what He did to the ancients who were opposing His religion and deviating from it, and what calamities He sends down upon the disbelievers if they persist in disbelief and cling to it, so that those who perish would perish after clear evidence, and those who live would live after clear evidence. And verily Allah is All-Hearing, All-Knowing. Now then: Indeed, the people of deviation and misguidance interpreted the Quran according to their opinions and explained it according to their whims, an interpretation for which Allah sent down no authority, nor did He clarify any proof, nor did they narrate it from the Messenger of the Lord of the worlds, nor from the pure members of his household, nor from the early predecessors among his Companions and the Successors. It is a fabrication against Allah; they have gone astray and were not rightly guided. They only took their interpretation from Abu Hudhayl, the seller of fodder, and his followers; and from Ibrahim al-Nazzam, the bead seller, and his imitators; and from al-Fuwati and his supporters; and from the one attributed to the village of Jubba and his claimants; and from al-Ashajj Ja'far ibn Harb and his followers; and from Ja'far ibn Mubashshir al-Qasabi and his bigots; and from al-Askafi, the ignorant, and his magnifiers; and from al-Farawi attributed to the city of Balkh and his followers. For they are the leaders of misguidance from the ignorant Mu'tazila, whom they made their religion and made them their support, relying upon them and making them their pillar. And I saw that al-Jubba'i wrote a book on the interpretation of the Quran, beginning it contrary to what Allah, Mighty and Majestic, revealed, and in the language of the people of his village known as Jubba, while he is not from the people of the tongue in which the Quran was revealed. He did not narrate in his book a single letter from any of the commentators, but relied on what his heart and his devil whispered to him. Were it not that he misled many of the common people with his book and brought many of the rabble down from the truth, there would be no justification for occupying myself with it. Al-Imam al-Hafiz Abu al-Qasim, may Allah be pleased with him, said: Then he mentioned some of the places where al-Jubba'i erred in his interpretation, and clarified where he erred in his interpretation of the Quran with the help and facilitation of Allah. All of this indicates his nobility, abundance of knowledge, and manifest virtue. May Allah reward him for his struggle in His religion with his tongue with the best reward and place him by His beneficence in the most sublime abode of His Garden.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a polemical introduction where Ibn Asakir, after praising the Quran and its miraculous nature, launches a fierce criticism against the Mu'tazila and their methods of tafsir. He first describes the perfection of the Quran: it is a clear proof, distinguishing truth from falsehood, containing abrogation, Meccan/Medinan, etc. He emphasizes that it is a miraculous revelation that the Arabs, despite their eloquence, could not imitate. Then he states that the people of deviation (ahl al-zaygh) interpreted the Quran according to their own opinions and whims, not based on transmitted authority from the Prophet, his family, or the Salaf. He names several early Mu'tazila figures—Abu Hudhayl, al-Nazzam, al-Fuwati, al-Jubba'i (from the village of Jubba), al-Ashajj Ja'far ibn Harb, Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, al-Askafi, and al-Farawi from Balkh—as sources of this corrupted tafsir, calling them leaders of misguidance. He specifically attacks al-Jubba'i's book of tafsir, noting that it is written in the dialect of his village (Jubba) rather than proper Arabic, and that it contains no transmitted reports from earlier commentators, relying solely on his own inner whisperings. Ibn Asakir admits he would not bother with it except that it has misled many common people. He then inserts a commendatory note (from the editor? actually it seems Ibn Asakir is quoting himself or an earlier authority) praising the scholar who refuted al-Jubba'i, indicating his nobility and knowledge. The passage thus establishes that Mu'tazila tafsir is based on personal opinion (ra'y) rather than transmission (riwaya) and is therefore invalid.

Key Terms
الزيغ
التضليل
التأويل
السلف
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what is the main source of Mu'tazila tafsir?
A) The Quran and Sunna
B) The opinions of the Salaf
C) Their own personal opinions and the teachings of their leaders
D) The Bible

Key Takeaway
Mu'tazila tafsir is rejected because it lacks transmission from the Salaf and relies on personal opinion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you open the Quran, do you ever catch yourself interpreting a verse in a way that suits your desires rather than how the Salaf understood it? What will you do today to ensure your interpretation is not based on your own whims?
?
Ibn Asakir names eight individuals who led others astray by their opinions. Are there any modern scholars or preachers you follow whose tafsir you haven't verified against the transmitted understanding of the Salaf? Will you commit to checking one interpretation this week?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed to follow reason, but Ibn Asakir says they had no proof from Allah, the Prophet, or the Salaf. When you face a verse that challenges your lifestyle or beliefs, do you submit to the transmitted meaning or do you twist it to fit your comfort? This lesson calls you to examine your heart: are you truly following the Quran or your own desires?

Al-Jubba'i's Tafsir: A Village Dialect and No Transmission
Ibn Asakir critiques al-Jubba'i's tafsir for linguistic and methodological errors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's specific criticisms of al-Jubba'i's tafsir, including its linguistic flaws and lack of scholarly authority.

Core Idea
Al-Jubba'i's tafsir is linguistically corrupt and devoid of transmitted reports.

After condemning the Mu'tazila collectively, Ibn Asakir focuses on one particularly influential figure: al-Jubba'i. He notes that al-Jubba'i wrote his tafsir in the dialect of his village, not in proper Arabic, and that it contains not a single transmitted report from earlier commentators. Despite its popularity among the common people, Ibn Asakir dismisses it as mere whispers of the heart and devil.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn Asakir's description of al-Jubba'i's book
Notice that he says the book begins contrary to what Allah revealed, and is written in the dialect of al-Jubba'i's village Jubba.
2
Identify the specific accusations
There are three main accusations: wrong language, no narrations from earlier commentators, and reliance on inner whispers.
3
Reflect on why Ibn Asakir bothered to refute it
He admits he would not have bothered except that the book misled many common people.
This shows the danger of such works.

The people of falsehood and slander and the refutation of what al-Jubba'i and al-Balkhi distorted in their books. He said in its beginning: Praise be to Allah, the Praiseworthy, the Glorious, the Beginner, the Restorer, the Doer of whatever He wills, who opened His book with His praise, and clarified in it His proof, and explained in it His lawful and His unlawful, and distinguished between truth and falsehood, and the knowledgeable and the ignorant, and sent it down as definitive and ambiguous, abrogating and abrogated, Meccan and Medinan, specific and general, and a parable set forth. He informed in it of the news of the ancients and the stories of the predecessors, and encouraged in it obedience, and warned and forbade in it from slips, transgressions, the steps of Satan, and misguidances. And He promised in it reward for those who act in obedience to Him for the Day of Return, and threatened in it those who disbelieve in it and avoid the truth and do not act obediently for the Day of Gathering and Reckoning. He made it an admonition for the believers, a lesson for those who come after, and a proof against the worlds, lest they say, 'Our Lord, why did You not send us a messenger so that we might follow Your verses and be among the believers?' He gathered in it the knowledge of the first and the last, and perfected in it the obligations and the religion. So it is the clear path of Allah and His strong rope. Whoever holds fast to it is saved, and whoever opposes it goes astray and errs and falls into ignorance. And He made it an Arabic Quran, without crookedness, in the tongue of the unlettered Arabs, to whom no messenger before him came from the Lord of the worlds with a book to recite to them in their tongue from the Originator of the heavens and the earths. And He cut off the excuse of the opponents of the prophethood of the Master of the Messengers, since He made it a miracle that they are incapable of producing the like of it, while they are masters of speech and utmost in eloquence. He made clear to them what they should do, what they should avoid, what is lawful, what is unlawful, and He clarified for them the paths of righteousness, guidance, and rectitude, and what He did to the ancients who were opposing His religion and deviating from it, and what calamities He sends down upon the disbelievers if they persist in disbelief and cling to it, so that those who perish would perish after clear evidence, and those who live would live after clear evidence. And verily Allah is All-Hearing, All-Knowing. Now then: Indeed, the people of deviation and misguidance interpreted the Quran according to their opinions and explained it according to their whims, an interpretation for which Allah sent down no authority, nor did He clarify any proof, nor did they narrate it from the Messenger of the Lord of the worlds, nor from the pure members of his household, nor from the early predecessors among his Companions and the Successors. It is a fabrication against Allah; they have gone astray and were not rightly guided. They only took their interpretation from Abu Hudhayl, the seller of fodder, and his followers; and from Ibrahim al-Nazzam, the bead seller, and his imitators; and from al-Fuwati and his supporters; and from the one attributed to the village of Jubba and his claimants; and from al-Ashajj Ja'far ibn Harb and his followers; and from Ja'far ibn Mubashshir al-Qasabi and his bigots; and from al-Askafi, the ignorant, and his magnifiers; and from al-Farawi attributed to the city of Balkh and his followers. For they are the leaders of misguidance from the ignorant Mu'tazila, whom they made their religion and made them their support, relying upon them and making them their pillar. And I saw that al-Jubba'i wrote a book on the interpretation of the Quran, beginning it contrary to what Allah, Mighty and Majestic, revealed, and in the language of the people of his village known as Jubba, while he is not from the people of the tongue in which the Quran was revealed. He did not narrate in his book a single letter from any of the commentators, but relied on what his heart and his devil whispered to him. Were it not that he misled many of the common people with his book and brought many of the rabble down from the truth, there would be no justification for occupying myself with it. Al-Imam al-Hafiz Abu al-Qasim, may Allah be pleased with him, said: Then he mentioned some of the places where al-Jubba'i erred in his interpretation, and clarified where he erred in his interpretation of the Quran with the help and facilitation of Allah. All of this indicates his nobility, abundance of knowledge, and manifest virtue. May Allah reward him for his struggle in His religion with his tongue with the best reward and place him by His beneficence in the most sublime abode of His Garden.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a polemical introduction where Ibn Asakir, after praising the Quran and its miraculous nature, launches a fierce criticism against the Mu'tazila and their methods of tafsir. He first describes the perfection of the Quran: it is a clear proof, distinguishing truth from falsehood, containing abrogation, Meccan/Medinan, etc. He emphasizes that it is a miraculous revelation that the Arabs, despite their eloquence, could not imitate. Then he states that the people of deviation (ahl al-zaygh) interpreted the Quran according to their own opinions and whims, not based on transmitted authority from the Prophet, his family, or the Salaf. He names several early Mu'tazila figures—Abu Hudhayl, al-Nazzam, al-Fuwati, al-Jubba'i (from the village of Jubba), al-Ashajj Ja'far ibn Harb, Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, al-Askafi, and al-Farawi from Balkh—as sources of this corrupted tafsir, calling them leaders of misguidance. He specifically attacks al-Jubba'i's book of tafsir, noting that it is written in the dialect of his village (Jubba) rather than proper Arabic, and that it contains no transmitted reports from earlier commentators, relying solely on his own inner whisperings. Ibn Asakir admits he would not bother with it except that it has misled many common people. He then inserts a commendatory note (from the editor? actually it seems Ibn Asakir is quoting himself or an earlier authority) praising the scholar who refuted al-Jubba'i, indicating his nobility and knowledge. The passage thus establishes that Mu'tazila tafsir is based on personal opinion (ra'y) rather than transmission (riwaya) and is therefore invalid.

تفسير
البلخى
العوام

Key Takeaway
Al-Jubba'i's tafsir is invalid because it was written in a non-standard Arabic dialect and contained no transmitted reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read or hear an Islamic teaching, do you check whether it has a reliable source (e.g., transmission from early scholars) or do you accept it because it sounds reasonable or comes from a known figure? Will you commit to verifying the chain of transmission before adopting a new understanding?
?
Al-Jubba'i relied on 'what his heart and his devil whispered' rather than transmitted knowledge. Are there any beliefs or practices you hold that come more from your desires or popular opinion than from authentic revelation? How will you begin to distinguish them?
?
Ibn Asakir considered al-Jubba'i's tafsir dangerous because it misled common people. Have you ever unknowingly accepted or shared a religious teaching that lacked proper basis? What will you do today to protect yourself and others from such errors?

Classification of Deviant Books and Praise of al-Ash'ari
Qadi al-Askar classifies books of philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima, noting al-Ash'ari's works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of deviant books on tawhid and the unique status of al-Ash'ari's works among them.

Core Idea
Not all books of theology are equal—some lead to destruction, others to truth.

Qadi al-Askar, a senior Hanafi scholar, reports his findings on the books written in the field of tawhid. He identifies three deviant categories and contrasts them with the prolific corpus of al-Ash'ari. This passage establishes a critical distinction between harmful and beneficial theological literature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing; then read the translation to grasp the overall classification.
The passage is a first-person report by Qadi al-Askar.
2
Identify the three forbidden categories
List the philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima. Note the specific names given for each group and the reasons they are forbidden.
Each category has a distinct prohibition: leading to destruction, causing doubts, or being the worst of innovators.
3
Contrast with al-Ash'ari
Observe how al-Ash'ari is described positively: many books, a comprehensive summary, and a work correcting the Mu'tazila. Understand that his books are implicitly acceptable.
Al-Ash'ari's earlier Mu'tazila affiliation explains why he wrote a book to correct them.
4
Reflect on the application
Consider why the early Salaf preserved some books and discarded others. This shows the importance of discernment in theological study.
The lesson is not that all kalam is forbidden, but that only sound, Sunni works are permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر أبو العباس المعروف بقاضى العسكر، وكان من كبراء أصحاب أبي حنيفة رضى الله عنه انه نظر فى كتب صنفها المتقدمون في علم التوحيد، قال فوجدت بعضها للفلاسفة مثل إسحق الكندي والاسفرازي وأمثالهما وذلك كله خارج عن الطريق المستقيم زائغ عن الدين القويم لا يجوز النظر فى تلك الكتب لانه يجر إلى المهالك لأنها مملؤة من الشرك والنفاق، مسماة باسم التوحيد، ولهذا ما امسك المتقدمون من أهل السنة والجماعة شيئا من كتبهم ووجدت تصانيف كثيرة في هذا الفن من العلم للمعتزلة مثل عبد الجبار الرازي والجبائي والكعبي والنظام وغيرهم، ولا يجوز امساك تلك الكتب ولا النظر فيها كيلا تحدث الشكوك ويوهن الاعتقاد ولئلا ينسب ممسكها إلى البدعة ولهذا ما امسكها المتقدمون من أهل السنة والجماعة فكذا المجسمة صنفوا كتبا في هذا الفن مثل محمد بن الهيصم وامثاله ولا يحل النظر فيها ولا امساكها فإنهم شر أهل البدع، وقد وقع في يدى بعض هذه التصانيف فما أمسكت منها شئيا، وقد وجدت الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه كتبا كثيرة في هذا الفن وهي قريبة من مائتى كتاب والموجز الكبير يأتي على عامة ما في كتبه وقد صنف الأشعرى كتابا كبيرا لتصحيح مذهب المعتزلة فإنه كان يعتقد مذهب
And Abu al-Abbas, known as Qadi al-Askar, who was among the senior companions of Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, mentioned that he examined books written by the early scholars on the science of tawhid. He said: I found some of them to be by philosophers, such as Ishaq al-Kindi and al-Asfarazi (al-Isfarayani?) and their like. All of that is outside the straight path, deviating from the upright religion. It is not permissible to look into those books because it leads to destruction, for they are filled with shirk and hypocrisy, named with the name of tawhid. For this reason, the early scholars of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a did not hold on to any of their books. And I found many writings in this art of knowledge by the Mu'tazila, such as Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi, al-Jubba'i, al-Ka'bi, al-Nazzam and others. It is not permissible to hold on to those books nor to look into them, lest doubts arise and belief be weakened, and lest the one who holds them be attributed to innovation. For this reason, the early scholars of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a did not hold on to them. Likewise, the Mujassima (anthropomorphists) wrote books in this art, such as Muhammad ibn al-Haysam and his like. It is not permissible to look into them nor to hold them, for they are the worst of the people of innovation. Some of these writings fell into my hands, but I did not keep any of them. And I found that al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, wrote many books in this art, close to two hundred books, and al-Mujaz al-Kabir covers most of what is in his books. And al-Ash'ari wrote a large book to correct the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, for he used to believe the doctrine
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a classification and ruling on various types of books on tawhid (divine unity) based on a report from Abu al-Abbas, known as Qadi al-Askar. He divides the books into three categories: 1) Books of philosophers (e.g., Ishaq al-Kindi, al-Asfarazi) – these are filled with shirk and hypocrisy, deviate from the straight path, and it is not permissible to look at them because they lead to destruction. The early Salaf did not preserve them. 2) Books of the Mu'tazila (e.g., Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi, al-Jubba'i, al-Ka'bi, al-Nazzam) – it is also not permissible to hold them or look into them because they create doubts and weaken correct belief, and holding them could lead to one being accused of innovation. Again, the Salaf did not keep them. 3) Books of the Mujassima (anthropomorphists, like Muhammad ibn al-Haysam) – they are the worst of the people of innovation, and their books are likewise forbidden to hold or study. The narrator (Qadi al-Askar) says that he personally came across some of these books but did not keep any. In contrast, he mentions al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (founder of the Ash'ari school) who wrote many books on this art (close to two hundred) and whose work 'al-Mujaz al-Kabir' summarizes his positions. Notably, al-Ash'ari wrote a large book to correct the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, implying his earlier Mu'tazila affiliation (before his conversion to Ahl al-Sunna). The passage thus establishes that the books of the three deviant groups are prohibited, while al-Ash'ari's books are implicitly acceptable (though not explicitly stated here), as they represent the correct Sunni doctrine.

Key Terms
الفلاسفة
المعتزلة
المجسمة
أبو الحسن الأشعري
التوحيد
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All books on kalam are equally forbidden.
Correction: The passage distinguishes deviant books (philosophers, Mu'tazila, Mujassima) from those of Ahl al-Sunna like al-Ash'ari, which are acceptable and valuable.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling according to Qadi al-Askar on books by philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima?
A) They are allowed for specialists
B) They are forbidden to hold or study because they lead to doubt and innovation
C) They are only allowed if studied with a teacher
D) They are acceptable as long as one is firm in faith

Key Takeaway
The passage establishes that theological books leading to false creeds are forbidden, while the works of Sunni scholars like al-Ash'ari are valuable and preserved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What books have you taken as sources for your creed? Have you ever read a book that you later realized contained shirk or hidden doubts? How did you respond, and what will you do differently after this lesson?
?
The early scholars did not hold onto deviant books, even for refutation. Are there any lectures or books you still consult that mix truth with falsehood? Will you remove them from your library or mind?
?
Al-Ash'ari wrote to correct error before teaching truth. Is your own understanding of tawhid built on refuting falsehood or on the sound foundations of Ahl al-Sunna? Which do you prioritize?
