Critique of al-Jubba'i's Tafsir and Praise of the Imam
Critique of al-Jubba'i's tafsir and praise of the Imam's corrections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the critique against al-Jubba'i's tafsir and the reasons for praising the Imam's corrections.

Core Idea
Al-Jubba'i's tafsir ignored the Quran's language and scholarly tradition.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's work presents a sharp condemnation of a Mu'tazili commentator and a heartfelt commendation of the Imam who corrected his errors. We will read the original Arabic, examine the specific accusations, and see how the Imam's responses demonstrate his scholarly merit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong language used against the Mu'tazila and al-Jubba'i.
2
Identify the two main sections
The passage has two clear parts: a critique of al-Jubba'i's tafsir and a praise of the Imam who corrected it. Find where the shift occurs.
The phrase 'قال الامام الحافظ أبو القسم' marks the beginning of the praise.
3
List the specific accusations against al-Jubba'i
The author gives several reasons for dismissing al-Jubba'i's tafsir. Write them down from the text.
Look for phrases like 'على خلاف ما أنزل الله' and 'على لغة أهل قريته'.
4
Reflect on the author's motivation
Why did the author bother to refute this tafsir? The passage states it was because it misled common people. Consider the responsibility of scholars to defend the truth.
5
Appreciate the prayer for the Imam
The passage ends with a du'a for the Imam. Reflect on what this tells us about the author's respect for him.
The prayer includes 'جهاده في دينه بلسانه' – jihad with the tongue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنسوب إلى مدينة بلخ وذويه فإنهم قادة الضلال من المعتزلة الجهال، الذين قلدوهم دينهم وجعلوهم معولهم، الذى عليه يعولون وركنهم الذى إليه يستندون ورأيت الجبائى ألف في تفسير القرآن كتابا أوله على خلاف ما أنزل الله عز وجل وعلى لغة أهل قريته المعروفة بجبى وليس من أهل اللسان الذي نزل به القرآن وماروى فى كتابه حرفا واحدا عن أحد من المفسرين وإنما اعتمد على ماوسوس به صدره وشيطانه ولولا انه استغوى بكتابه كثيرا من العوام واستنزل به عن الحق كثيرا من الطغام، لم يكن لتشاغلی به وجه . قال الامام الحافظ أبو القسم رضى الله عنه ثم ذكر بعض المواضع التي اخطأ فيها الجبائى فى تفسيره، وبين ما اخطأ فيه من تأويل القرآن بعون الله له وتيسيره وكل ذلك مما يدل على نبله وكثرة علمه وظهور فضله، فجزاه الله على جهاده في دينه بلسانه الحسنى وأحله باحسانه في مستقر جنانه المحل الأسنى .
Those attributed to the city of Balkh and its people, for they are the leaders of misguidance from the ignorant Mu'tazila, who have imitated them in their religion and made them their reliance, the support upon which they depend and the pillar to which they cling. And I saw that al-Jubba'i authored a book on the interpretation of the Qur'an, beginning it contrary to what Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, revealed, and upon the language of the people of his village known as Jubba, and he is not from the people of the tongue in which the Qur'an was revealed. And he did not narrate in his book a single letter from any of the commentators. Rather, he relied on what his heart and his devil whispered to him. And were it not that his book had seduced many of the common people and brought down many of the rabble from the truth, I would not have occupied myself with it. The Imam, the Hafiz, Abu al-Qasim (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Then he mentioned some of the places in which al-Jubba'i erred in his tafsir, and explained what he erred in regarding the interpretation of the Qur'an, with the help and facilitation of Allah. And all of that indicates his nobility, the abundance of his knowledge, and the manifestation of his virtue. May Allah reward him for his jihad in His religion with his tongue, the best reward, and settle him, by His goodness, in the abode of His Paradise, the highest station.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage begins with a condemnation of the Mu'tazila of Balkh, calling them leaders of misguidance. It then focuses on al-Jubba'i, a Mu'tazili scholar, and his tafsir. The author criticizes al-Jubba'i for composing a commentary that contradicts the Quran's revelation and relies on the dialect of his village (Jubba) rather than the classical Arabic of the Quran. Moreover, al-Jubba'i ignored all earlier commentators, relying instead on his own whims and satanic inspirations. The author only engaged with this book because it misled many common people. Then the Imam (likely Ibn 'Asakir) is praised for identifying and correcting al-Jubba'i's errors, which demonstrates the Imam's knowledge and virtue. The passage ends with a prayer for the Imam.

Key Terms
الجبائي
التفسير
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author criticizes all Mu'tazila equally.
Correction: The criticism is specifically targeted at al-Jubba'i's tafsir methodology, not the entire sect, though he does call the Balkh Mu'tazila leaders of misguidance.

Checkpoint
What is the main criticism of al-Jubba'i's tafsir in this passage?
A) He relied on weak hadiths.
B) He interpreted the Quran based on his own dialect and not the classical Arabic of the Quran.
C) He included too many philosophical arguments.
D) He plagiarized from earlier works.

Key Takeaway
This passage demonstrates that proper tafsir must adhere to the Quran's language and rely on the interpretations of the early scholars, and that defending orthodoxy is a virtuous jihad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted an interpretation of the Quran simply because it was popular or came from a charismatic speaker, without verifying that it aligns with the Quran's language and the understanding of the early scholars? What will you do differently now?
?
The author only engaged with al-Jubba'i's book because it misled many people. Is there a false teaching you have encountered but ignored, thinking it was not your responsibility? Are there people being misled around you whom you could help by speaking the truth?
?
The Imam's correction of errors is called jihad with his tongue. How often do you use your tongue to defend the truth, even when it is unpopular? What one step can you take this week to make your speech a form of jihad for Allah's religion?

Al-Ash'ari's Stance on Innovators and His Deathbed Testimony
Chapter heading and two deathbed narrations about al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's balance of opposing innovators while refusing to excommunicate Muslims of the qibla.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari cursed the Mu'tazila but refused to takfir any Muslim.

This lesson presents two deathbed statements from Imam al-Ash'ari that illustrate his approach to sectarian disputes. While he vigorously opposed the Mu'tazila, he also maintained that Muslims who pray toward the Kaaba are not to be declared disbelievers. These statements together show his commitment to orthodox creed and his refusal to fall into extremism.

Guided Path
1
Read the chapter heading and first narration
Notice how the chapter sets the theme of avoiding innovators. Then read the first deathbed report where al-Ash'ari curses the Mu'tazila.
This shows his opposition to a specific innovating group.
2
Read the second narration
Here al-Ash'ari testifies he does not excommunicate people of the qibla. Pay attention to his reasoning: because all worship the same God.
This qualifies his earlier curse, showing he distinguishes between groups and individuals.
3
Reflect on the consistency
Consider how these two statements together demonstrate his balanced approach: opposing theological errors without takfir of the masses.
This is a key principle in Sunni orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما وصف من مجانبته لأهل البدع وجهاده وذكر ما عرف من نصيحته للأمة وصحة اعتقاده أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن الفضل الفراوي بنيسابور قال سمعت الاستاذ ابا القسم عبد الملك بن هوازن القشيري يقول سمعت الاستاذ الشهيد ابا على الحسن بن على الدقاق رحمه الله يقول : سمعت ابا على زاهر بن أحمد الفقيه رحمه الله يقول مات أبو الحسن الأشعري رحمه الله ورأسه في حجرى وكان يقول شيئا في حال نزعه من داخل حلقه فادنيت إليه رأسى وأصغيت إلى ما كان يقرع سمعى فكان يقول : لعن الله المعتزلة موهوا ومخرقوا، سمعت الشيخين ابا محمد عبد الجبار بن أحمد بن. محمد البيهقى الفقيه وابا القسم زاهر بن طاهر المعدل بنيسابور يقولان سمعنا الشيخ ابا بكر أحمد بن الحسين بن على البيهقى يقول سمعت ابا حازم عمر بن أحمد العبدوى الحافظ يقول سمعت ابا على زاهر بن أحمد السرخسي، يقول لما قرب حضور أجل أبي الحسن الأشعري رحمه الله في داری ببغداد دعانى فأتيته فقال اشهد على انى لا أكفر أحدا من أهل هذه القبلة لأن الكل يشيرون إلى معبود واحد وإنما هذا كله اختلاف العبارات .
Chapter on what is described of his avoidance of the people of innovation and his striving, and mention of what was known of his sincere advice to the community and the soundness of his belief. Shaykh Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi informed us in Nishapur, he said: I heard the master Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Malik ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri say: I heard the martyr master Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq (may Allah have mercy on him) say: I heard Abu Ali Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Faqih (may Allah have mercy on him) say: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah have mercy on him) died while his head was in my lap, and he was saying something in the throes of death from inside his throat, so I brought my ear close to him and listened to what was striking my hearing, and he was saying: May Allah curse the Mu'tazila, they deceived and fabricated. I heard the two shaykhs Abu Muhammad Abd al-Jabbar ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Bayhaqi the jurist and Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir al-Mu'addil in Nishapur saying: We heard Shaykh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Bayhaqi say: I heard Abu Hazim Umar ibn Ahmad al-Abdawi al-Hafiz say: I heard Abu Ali Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi say: When the presence of the term of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah have mercy on him) drew near, in my house in Baghdad, he summoned me, so I came to him, and he said: Bear witness for me that I do not declare anyone of this qibla a disbeliever, because all point to one worshipped, and this is only a difference of expressions.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage begins with a chapter heading that announces the topic: al-Ash'ari's avoidance of innovators, his struggle, his sincere advice to the community, and the soundness of his belief. The heading is followed by two deathbed narrations. The first, through al-Qushayri and al-Daqqaq, reports that al-Ash'ari, with his head in the lap of Abu Ali Zahir al-Faqih, uttered a curse against the Mu'tazila, saying 'May Allah curse the Mu'tazila, they deceived and fabricated.' The second narration, through al-Bayhaqi, reports that al-Ash'ari, near death, called Abu Ali Zahir al-Sarakhsi and testified that he does not declare anyone of the people of the qibla (i.e., Muslims) a disbeliever, because all point to one object of worship, and differences are only in expressions. Together, these statements show al-Ash'ari's intense opposition to the Mu'tazila while maintaining that Muslims who pray toward the Kaaba are not to be excommunicated.

Key Terms
أهل البدع
المعتزلة
لا أكفر أحدا من أهل هذه القبلة
اختلاف العبارات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's curse of the Mu'tazila contradicts his refusal to takfir Ahl al-Qibla.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari distinguishes between condemning a sect and excommunicating individual Muslims; his curse targets the group, but he affirms that all who pray toward the Kaaba are believers regardless of theological differences.

Checkpoint
What did al-Ash'ari testify on his deathbed regarding Muslims?
A) He cursed all who follow their own opinion
B) He declared that all Muslims are disbelievers
C) He said he does not declare any person of the qibla a disbeliever
D) He said only his followers are saved

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari opposed the Mu'tazila but affirmed the unity of all Muslims who pray toward the Kaaba.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disagree with a fellow Muslim's understanding of Islam, do your words and heart still respect their qibla? What would change in your relationships if you took al-Ash'ari's deathbed testimony personally?
?
Al-Ash'ari's final act was to testify against takfir. If you could only leave one legacy before you die, would it be about who you excluded or who you refused to exclude?
?
Think of someone whose beliefs you find seriously wrong. Can you honestly say, like al-Ash'ari, that you neither excommunicate them in your heart nor abandon the truth you hold? What is preventing that balance in you?

The Ash'ari Position on the Sahaba's Ijtihad
Ibn Asakir presents Ash'ari's position that all Companions were correct in their ijtihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari reconciled the disagreements among the Companions by affirming the validity and reward of their ijtihad.

Core Idea
All mujtahid Sahaba are correct and rewarded for their ijtihad.

The early Muslim community witnessed significant disagreements among the Companions after the Prophet's death. Various sects emerged, each taking extreme positions on the status of key figures like 'Uthman, 'Ali, Mu'awiya, and 'A'isha. In this passage, Ibn 'Asakir presents al-Ash'ari's balanced approach, which avoids condemning any of the Companions and instead upholds the validity of their ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once to understand the flow of Ibn Asakir's presentation. Notice how he lists the views of four sects before stating al-Ash'ari's position.
2
Identify the four sectarian positions
Identify what each group (Khawarij, Mu'tazila, Rafida, Umawiyya) said about the Companions involved in the early conflicts. Note the extreme nature of each claim.
3
Understand al-Ash'ari's middle way
Focus on the statement: 'So he followed a middle way among them and said: Every mujtahid is correct.' Reflect on how this upholds the integrity of all Companions while acknowledging their differences.
Al-Ash'ari distinguishes between differences in fundamentals (usul) and subsidiary matters (furu').
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this position is important for Sunni theology and how it fosters respect for all Sahaba. Note that it does not claim infallibility but validates sincere ijtihad.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you grasp the key point: why al-Ash'ari considers all mujtahid Companions correct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك قالت الخوارج بكفر عثمان وعلى رضى الله عنهما ونص الله [؟] هر رضی عنه على موالاتهما وتفضيل المقدم على المؤخر، وكذلك قالت المعتزلة ان أمير المؤمنين معاوية وطلحة والزبير وام المؤمنين عائشة وكل من تبعهم رضى الله على الخطأ ولو شهدوا كلهم بحبة واحدة لم تقبل شهادتهم وقالت الرافضة ان هؤلاء كلهم كفار ارتدوا بعد إسلامهم وبعضهم لم يسلموا وقالت الأموية لايجوز عليهم الخطأ بحال فسلك رضى عنه طريقة بينهم وقال كل مجتهد مصيب وكلهم على الحق وإنهم لم يختلفوا في الأصول وإنما اختلفوا في الفروع ، فأدى اجتهاد كل واحد منهم إلى شيء فهو مصيب وله الأجر والثواب على ذلك
And likewise the Khawarij said: 'Uthman and 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with them, are disbelievers, and Allah's text (?) [unclear] ... upon loyalty to both of them and preferring the forefront over the later. And likewise the Mu'tazila said: Indeed, the Commander of the Faithful Mu'awiya, Talha, al-Zubayr, the Mother of the Believers 'A'isha, and all who followed them—may Allah be pleased with them—were upon error, and if they all testified about a single grain, their testimony would not be accepted. And the Rafida said: These all are disbelievers who apostatized after their Islam, and some of them never even submitted. And the Umawiyya said: Error is not possible for them at all. So he, may Allah be pleased with him, followed a middle way among them and said: Every mujtahid is correct (musib), and all of them are upon the truth; they did not differ in fundamentals (usul) but only in subsidiary matters (furu'); so the ijtihad of each one led him to something, and he is correct, and he has reward and recompense for that.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage addresses the historical disagreements among the Companions (Sahaba) after the Prophet's death, especially regarding the caliphate of 'Uthman and 'Ali. The Khawarij declared both 'Uthman and 'Ali disbelievers. The Mu'tazila held that Mu'awiya, Talha, al-Zubayr, 'A'isha and their followers were in error, so their testimony is invalid. The Rafida (extreme Shi'a) claimed these Companions all became apostates, and some never even accepted Islam. The Umawiyya (those who defended the Umayyad side) claimed that these Companions could not err at all. Al-Ash'ari's middle way states that every mujtahid among them is correct (musib): they did not differ in the fundamental principles of religion (usul) but only in subsidiary matters (furu') where ijtihad is valid. Each one followed his ijtihad and is rewarded for it. This upholds the justice and integrity of all major figures of early Islam.

Key Terms
الخوارج
المعتزلة
الرافضة
الأموية
مجتهد
مصيب
الأصول
الفروع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari claimed all Sahaba were infallible and never made mistakes.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari taught that their ijtihad was correct and rewarded, not that they were infallible in all actions. He acknowledged differences in subsidiary matters (furu').

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, why should we consider all Companions who engaged in ijtihad as correct?
A) Because they were infallible and never made mistakes.
B) Because their differences were in fundamental matters (usul).
C) Because their differences were in subsidiary matters (furu') and each followed his best judgment.
D) Because the Khawarij and Rafida were wrong about them.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's middle way affirms that all mujtahid Companions are correct and rewarded for their ijtihad, preserving their integrity while acknowledging differences in subsidiary matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the early conflicts among the Sahaba, do you find yourself internally taking sides or holding judgments against any of them? This lesson teaches that Ash'ari considered every mujtahid among them correct and rewarded. Are you willing to surrender your own judgments and entrust their matter entirely to Allah, accepting that their ijtihad was sincere and accepted?
?
Before studying this lesson, which of the five positions—Khawarij, Mu'tazila, Rafida, Umawiyya, or Ash'ari—most closely matched your own attitude toward the Companions? Are you guilty of leaning toward one of the extremes, either condemning some or insisting on infallibility? What would it cost you to adopt the middle way, and are you ready to pay that price?
?
Consider a current disagreement you have with a fellow Muslim. Is it about a fundamental principle of faith (usul) or a subsidiary matter (furu')? If it is subsidiary, are you willing to treat that person as a mujtahid who is correct and rewarded, even if you remain convinced your own view is right? This lesson forces you to lower your certainty in your own ijtihad. Can you do that, and what would change in your heart if you did?

Al-Ash'ari's Balanced View on Intercession
Al-Ash'ari's middle path on prophetic intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's position on prophetic intercession as a middle path between absolute denial and unrestricted affirmation, grounded in divine permission.

Core Idea
Prophetic intercession is real but only by Allah's permission for those He approves.

Before al-Ash'ari, the Mu'tazila denied intercession entirely, while others may have exaggerated it. Al-Ash'ari navigated between these extremes by affirming intercession for believers who deserve punishment, but only by Allah's command and for those He approves. This lesson presents his balanced stance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on intercession
Read the Arabic passage about intercession and its translation. Notice how al-Ash'ari responds to the Mu'tazila position.
The Mu'tazila denied intercession completely.
2
Identify the key conditions
Al-Ash'ari places conditions on intercession: it is for believers who deserve punishment, by Allah's permission, and only for those He approves. Note these three conditions.
3
Reflect on the middle path
Consider why this is a middle path. It neither denies intercession nor affirms it without limits. Think about how this reflects al-Ash'ari's methodology.
This connects to the broader theme of balance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنهم قبلت وقالت المعتزلة لاشفاعة له بحال، فسلك رضى الله عنه طريقة بينهما. فقال بأن للرسول صلوات الله عليه وسلامه شفاعة مقبولة في المؤمنين المستحقين للعقوبة، يشفع لهم بأمر الله تعالى وإذنه ولا يشفع إلا لمن ارتضى. وكذلك قالت الخوارج بكفر عثمان وعلي رضى الله عنهما ونص الله هر[؟] رضی عنه على موالاتهما وتفضيل المقدم على المؤخر. وكذلك قالت المعتزلة ان أمير المؤمنين معاوية وطلحة والزبير وام المؤمنين عائشة وكل من تبعهم رضى الله على الخطأ ولو شهدوا كلهم بحبة واحدة لم تقبل شهادتهم. وقالت الرافضة ان هؤلاء كلهم كفار ارتدوا بعد إسلامهم وبعضهم لم يسلموا. وقالت الأموية لايجوز عليهم الخطأ بحال فسلك رضى عنه طريقة بينهم وقال كل مجتهد مصيب وكلهم على الحق وإنهم لم يختلفوا في الأصول وإنما اختلفوا في الفروع، فأدى اجتهاد كل واحد منهم إلى شيء فهو مصيب وله الأجر والثواب على ذلك. إلى غير ذلك من أصول يكثر تعدادها وتذكارها. وهذه الطرق التي سلكها لم يسلكها شهوة وإرادة، ولم يحدثها بدعة واستحسانا ولكنه أثبتها ببراهين عقلية مخبورة وأدلة شرعية مسبورة وأعلام هادية إلى الحق وحجج داعية إلى الصواب والصدق، هي الطرق إلى الله سبحانه وتعالى والسبيل إلى النجاة والفوز من تمسك بها فاز ونجا ومن حاد عنها ضل وغوى.
Before him, the Mu'tazila said: There is no intercession for him at all. So Abu al-Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him) followed a middle way between them. He said: The Messenger (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) has accepted intercession for the believers who deserve punishment; he intercedes for them by the command of Allah and His permission, and he only intercedes for those whom He approves. Likewise, the Khawarij said that 'Uthman and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both) are disbelievers, and [؟] God supported him[؟] (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding their loyalty and preferring the earlier over the later. Likewise, the Mu'tazila said that the Commander of the Faithful Mu'awiya, Talha, al-Zubayr, and the Mother of the Believers 'Aisha, and all who followed them (may Allah be pleased with them) are in error, and if all of them together testified to a single grain, their testimony would not be accepted. The Rawafid said that all of these are disbelievers who apostatized after their Islam, and some of them never became Muslims. The Umawiyya said that error cannot befall them at all. So he (may Allah be pleased with him) followed a middle way among them and said: Every mujtahid is correct, and all of them are upon the truth, and they did not differ in principles but rather differed in branches. The ijtihad of each of them led him to something, so he is correct and has reward and recompense for that. And there are other principles too numerous to count and mention. These methods that he followed were not followed out of desire or will, nor did he initiate them as innovation or approval; rather, he established them by probed rational proofs and measured legal evidences, guiding signs to the truth, and proofs calling to rightness and truth. They are the paths to Allah, the Exalted, and the way to salvation and success. Whoever holds fast to them succeeds and is saved, and whoever deviates from them goes astray and is ruined.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage defines al-Ash'ari's method of taking a middle path between extremist sects. Ibn Asakir begins by stating that before al-Ash'ari, the Mu'tazila denied intercession entirely. Al-Ash'ari balanced this by saying intercession is for believers who deserve punishment, by Allah's permission and only for those He approves. Similarly, on the companions, the Khawarij declared 'Uthman and 'Ali disbelievers, the Mu'tazila declared the other companions (Mu'awiya, Talha, etc.) to be in error and their testimony invalid, the Rawafid declared them all apostates, and the Umawiyya claimed they were infallible. Al-Ash'ari took the position that all mujtahids among the companions are correct; they differed only in subsidiary matters, not in principles. Each attained what his ijtihad led him to, and each has reward. Ibn Asakir emphasizes that al-Ash'ari did not invent these views out of desire or innovation, but established them with rational proofs and legal evidences. The passage concludes by declaring these paths as the true way to Allah and salvation.

Key Terms
شفاعة
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Ash'ari say about the intercession of the Prophet?
A) He denied it entirely.
B) He affirmed it unconditionally.
C) He said it is for believers who deserve punishment, by Allah's permission.
D) He said it is only for sinners.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirmed prophetic intercession for believers who deserve punishment, by Allah's permission and for those He approves, as a middle path.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that being a Muslim alone guarantees you the Prophet's intercession, regardless of your actions? How does al-Ash'ari's condition 'only for those whom He approves' make you reconsider your reliance on that hope? What will you change today to be among those whom Allah approves?
?
The Mu'tazila denied intercession to prevent complacency. Do you ever use the hope of intercession as an excuse to delay repentance? Reflect on a specific sin you have normalized, and commit to abandoning it starting today, knowing that intercession is not automatic.

Al-Ash'ari's Balanced View on the Companions and His Method
Al-Ash'ari's middle path on the companions and his evidence-based methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's position that all companions are correct in their ijtihad and that he based his views on rational and legal proofs.

Core Idea
Every companion-mujtahid is correct; their differences are in branches, not principles.

Various sects took extreme positions on the companions of the Prophet. Al-Ash'ari offered a middle way that upholds the honor of all companions while acknowledging their differences as valid ijtihad. He also emphasizes that his method is not based on desire but on evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the companions
Read the Arabic passage about the companions and its translation. Notice the four positions al-Ash'ari mentions before his own.
These are the positions of Khawarij, Mu'tazila, Rawafid, and Umawiyya.
2
Identify al-Ash'ari's response
Al-Ash'ari says every mujtahid is correct and all are upon the truth. He explains that their differences were in subsidiary matters, not principles.
This is the key to his middle path.
3
Understand the methodological statement
Al-Ash'ari did not follow these views out of desire but established them with rational proofs and legal evidences. Reflect on the importance of evidence-based theology.
This shows his commitment to scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنهم قبلت وقالت المعتزلة لاشفاعة له بحال، فسلك رضى الله عنه طريقة بينهما. فقال بأن للرسول صلوات الله عليه وسلامه شفاعة مقبولة في المؤمنين المستحقين للعقوبة، يشفع لهم بأمر الله تعالى وإذنه ولا يشفع إلا لمن ارتضى. وكذلك قالت الخوارج بكفر عثمان وعلي رضى الله عنهما ونص الله هر[؟] رضی عنه على موالاتهما وتفضيل المقدم على المؤخر. وكذلك قالت المعتزلة ان أمير المؤمنين معاوية وطلحة والزبير وام المؤمنين عائشة وكل من تبعهم رضى الله على الخطأ ولو شهدوا كلهم بحبة واحدة لم تقبل شهادتهم. وقالت الرافضة ان هؤلاء كلهم كفار ارتدوا بعد إسلامهم وبعضهم لم يسلموا. وقالت الأموية لايجوز عليهم الخطأ بحال فسلك رضى عنه طريقة بينهم وقال كل مجتهد مصيب وكلهم على الحق وإنهم لم يختلفوا في الأصول وإنما اختلفوا في الفروع، فأدى اجتهاد كل واحد منهم إلى شيء فهو مصيب وله الأجر والثواب على ذلك. إلى غير ذلك من أصول يكثر تعدادها وتذكارها. وهذه الطرق التي سلكها لم يسلكها شهوة وإرادة، ولم يحدثها بدعة واستحسانا ولكنه أثبتها ببراهين عقلية مخبورة وأدلة شرعية مسبورة وأعلام هادية إلى الحق وحجج داعية إلى الصواب والصدق، هي الطرق إلى الله سبحانه وتعالى والسبيل إلى النجاة والفوز من تمسك بها فاز ونجا ومن حاد عنها ضل وغوى.
Before him, the Mu'tazila said: There is no intercession for him at all. So Abu al-Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him) followed a middle way between them. He said: The Messenger (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) has accepted intercession for the believers who deserve punishment; he intercedes for them by the command of Allah and His permission, and he only intercedes for those whom He approves. Likewise, the Khawarij said that 'Uthman and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both) are disbelievers, and [؟] God supported him[؟] (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding their loyalty and preferring the earlier over the later. Likewise, the Mu'tazila said that the Commander of the Faithful Mu'awiya, Talha, al-Zubayr, and the Mother of the Believers 'Aisha, and all who followed them (may Allah be pleased with them) are in error, and if all of them together testified to a single grain, their testimony would not be accepted. The Rawafid said that all of these are disbelievers who apostatized after their Islam, and some of them never became Muslims. The Umawiyya said that error cannot befall them at all. So he (may Allah be pleased with him) followed a middle way among them and said: Every mujtahid is correct, and all of them are upon the truth, and they did not differ in principles but rather differed in branches. The ijtihad of each of them led him to something, so he is correct and has reward and recompense for that. And there are other principles too numerous to count and mention. These methods that he followed were not followed out of desire or will, nor did he initiate them as innovation or approval; rather, he established them by probed rational proofs and measured legal evidences, guiding signs to the truth, and proofs calling to rightness and truth. They are the paths to Allah, the Exalted, and the way to salvation and success. Whoever holds fast to them succeeds and is saved, and whoever deviates from them goes astray and is ruined.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage defines al-Ash'ari's method of taking a middle path between extremist sects. Ibn Asakir begins by stating that before al-Ash'ari, the Mu'tazila denied intercession entirely. Al-Ash'ari balanced this by saying intercession is for believers who deserve punishment, by Allah's permission and only for those He approves. Similarly, on the companions, the Khawarij declared 'Uthman and 'Ali disbelievers, the Mu'tazila declared the other companions (Mu'awiya, Talha, etc.) to be in error and their testimony invalid, the Rawafid declared them all apostates, and the Umawiyya claimed they were infallible. Al-Ash'ari took the position that all mujtahids among the companions are correct; they differed only in subsidiary matters, not in principles. Each attained what his ijtihad led him to, and each has reward. Ibn Asakir emphasizes that al-Ash'ari did not invent these views out of desire or innovation, but established them with rational proofs and legal evidences. The passage concludes by declaring these paths as the true way to Allah and salvation.

Key Terms
الخوارج
المعتزلة
الرافضة
الأموية
مجتهد
اجتهاد
براهين عقلية
أدلة شرعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, why are the companions' differences acceptable?
A) They were infallible.
B) They differed in principles.
C) They differed only in branches and each is correct.
D) Their differences are not valid.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirmed that all companion-mujtahids are correct, differing only in branches, and that his positions are based on solid evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a difference of opinion among scholars you respect, do you instinctively choose the view that suits your desires, or do you seek evidence as al-Ash'ari did? What one step can you take today to change that habit?
?
Al-Ash'ari affirmed that every companion-mujtahid is correct and rewarded. Is there a companion you have criticized or doubted in your heart? Will you repent and adopt this balanced view?
?
The passage says al-Ash'ari's method was based on rational proofs and legal evidences, not desire. Are your beliefs in Islamic theology built on solid evidence or blind tradition? What will you do to ensure they are grounded in proof?

Sects and Disagreements

Refuting Denial of Vision, Intercession, and Grave Punishment
Ibn Asakir lists three Qadariyya denials and cites consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir refutes the Qadariyya's rejection of three core Sunni beliefs—seeing Allah in the Hereafter, the Prophet's intercession, and the punishment of the grave—by appealing to transmitted reports and consensus.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya denied the seen, intercession, and grave—but the Companions agreed on them.

Ibn Asakir begins his refutation of the Qadariyya by exposing their fundamental error: they followed their own opinions and rejected the transmitted teachings of the Prophet and his Companions. In this passage, he focuses on three specific beliefs they denied: the believers' vision of Allah in the Hereafter, the Prophet's intercession, and the punishment of the grave. He emphasizes that these were established by numerous reports and the consensus of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the specific accusations Ibn Asakir levels against the Qadariyya.
Notice the tone: Ibn Asakir lists these denials as clear contradictions to transmitted evidence.
2
Identify the three denials
Locate where Ibn Asakir explicitly mentions their denial of seeing Allah (رؤية الله), intercession (شفاعة), and punishment of the grave (عذاب القبر).
He uses the verb 'أنكروا' (they denied) for each.
3
Reflect on the method of refutation
Ibn Asakir does not provide detailed rational arguments here; he simply asserts that these beliefs are established by multiple chains of transmission (تواترت بها الآثار) and consensus (أجمع على ذلك الصحابة والتابعون). Consider why this is effective against a group that claims to follow reason over tradition.
This shows the importance of transmitted knowledge (naql) in Sunni theology.
4
Connect to the broader refutation
Understand that these three denials are just the beginning; the passage continues with more errors. This lesson sets the stage for the rest of Ibn Asakir's refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك أن الله وأهل القدر مالت بهم أهواؤهم إلى التقليد لرؤسائهم ومن مضى من أسلافهم فتأولوا القرآن على آرائهم تأويلا لم ينزل الله به سلطانا ولا أوضح به برهانا، ولا نقلوه عن رسول رب العالمين ولا عن السلف المتقدمين فخالفوا رواية الصحابة عن نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رؤية الله بالأبصار، وقد جاءت في ذلك الروايات من الجهات المختلفات وتواترت بها الآثار وتتابعت بها الأخبار وأنكروا شفاعة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وردوا الرواية عن السلف المتقدمين وجحدوا عذاب القبر وأن الكفار في قبورهم يعذبون وقد أجمع على ذلك الصحابة والتابعون ودانوا بخلق القرآن نظيرا لقول إخوانهم من المشركين الذين قالوا إن هذا إلا قول البشر، فزعموا أن القرآن كقول البشر وأثبتوا وأيقنوا أن العباد يخلقون الشر نظيرا لقول المجوس الذين يثبتون خالقين أحدهما يخلق الخير والآخر يخلق الشر، وزعمت القدرية أن الله تعالى يخلق الخير وأن الشيطان يخلق الشر وزعموا أن الله عز وجل يشاء ما لا يكون ويكون ما لا يشاء خلافا لما أجمع عليه المسلمون من أن ما شاء الله كان وما لا يشاء لا يكون وردا لقول الله (وما تشاءون إلا أن يشاء الله) فاخبر أنا لا نشاء شيئا إلا وقد شاء أن نشاءه أو لقوله (ولو شاء الله ما اقتتلوا) ولقوله (ولو شئنا لآتينا كل نفس هداها) ولقوله تعالى (فعال لما يريد) ولقوله مخبرا عن شعيب إنه قال (وما يكون لنا أن نعود فيها إلا أن يشاء الله ربنا) ولهذا سماهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مجوس هذه الأمة لأنهم دانوا بديانة المجوس وضاهوا أقوالهم وزعموا أن للخير والشر خالقين كما زعمت المجوس وأنه يكون من الشر ما لا يشاء الله كما قالت المجوس ذلك وزعموا أنهم يملكون الضر والنفع لأنفسهم ردا لقول الله تعالى (قل لا أملك لنفسي ضرا ولا نفعا إلا ما شاء الله) وانحرافا عن القرآن وعما أجمع المسلمون عليه وزعموا أنهم ينفردون بالقدرة على أعمالهم دون ربهم وأثبتوا لأنفسهم غنى عن الله عز وجل، ووصفوا أنفسهم بالقدرة على ما لم يصفوا الله بالقدرة عليه، كما أثبت المجوس للشيطان من القدرة على الشر ما لم يثبتوه الله عز وجل فكانوا مجوس هذه الأمة إذ دانوا بديانة المجوس وتمسكوا بأقوالهم ومالوا إلى أضاليلهم وقنطوا الناس من رحمة الله تعالى وأيسوهم من روحه وحكموا على العصاة بالنار والخلود خلافا لقول الله تعالى (ويغفر ما دون ذلك لمن يشاء) وزعموا أن من دخل النار لا يخرج منها خلافا لما جاءت به الرواية عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن الله عز وجل يخرج من النار قوما بعد ما امتحشوا فيها وصاروا حمما ودفعوا أن يكون لله وجه مع قوله (ويبقى وجه ربك ذو الجلال والإكرام) وأنكروا أن يكون لله يدان مع قوله (لما خلقت بيدي) وأنكروا أن يكون له عين مع قوله (تجري بأعيننا) ولقوله (ولتصنع على عيني) ونفوا ما روي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من قوله (إن الله ينزل إلى السماء الدنيا) وأنا ذاكر ذلك إن شاء الله بابا بابا وبه المعونة والتأييد ومنه التوفيق والتسديد
That is because the people of Qadr (Qadariyya) were led by their desires to imitate their leaders and those who passed from their predecessors, so they interpreted the Qur'an according to their opinions, an interpretation for which Allah sent down no authority and made clear no proof, and they did not transmit it from the Messenger of the Lord of the Worlds nor from the earlier predecessors. So they contradicted the transmission of the Companions from the Prophet of Allah (peace be upon him) concerning seeing Allah with the eyes, and the reports have come about that from various directions, and the narrations have been transmitted successively, and the traditions have followed one after another. And they denied the intercession of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), rejected the transmission from the earlier predecessors, denied the punishment of the grave and that the disbelievers are punished in their graves, though the Companions and the Successors have agreed upon that. And they professed the creation of the Qur'an, analogous to the saying of their brothers from the polytheists who said, 'This is nothing but the words of a human being.' So they claimed that the Qur'an is like human speech. And they affirmed and believed that the servants create evil, analogous to the saying of the Magians who affirm two creators, one creating good and the other creating evil. And the Qadariyya claimed that Allah the Exalted creates good and that Satan creates evil, and they claimed that Allah the Exalted wills what does not happen and what He does not will happens, contrary to what the Muslims have agreed upon—that whatever Allah wills happens, and what He does not will does not happen—and in rejection of the saying of Allah: 'And you do not will unless Allah wills' (Q 76:30), for He informed that we do not will anything unless He has willed that we will it; or of His saying: 'And if Allah had willed, they would not have fought' (Q 2:253); and His saying: 'And if We had willed, We could have guided every soul' (Q 32:13); and His saying the Exalted: 'Doer of whatever He wills' (Q 85:16); and His saying, informing about Shu'ayb: 'And it is not for us to return to it unless Allah, our Lord, wills' (Q 7:89). For this reason, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) called them the Magians of this community, because they followed the religion of the Magians and resembled their sayings. And they claimed that there are two creators for good and evil, just as the Magians claimed, and that there occurs from evil what Allah does not will, as the Magians said that. And they claimed that they possess harm and benefit for themselves, in rejection of the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Say: I do not possess for myself harm or benefit except what Allah wills' (Q 7:188), and in deviation from the Qur'an and from what the Muslims have agreed upon. And they claimed that they are independent in power over their actions without their Lord, and they affirmed for themselves independence from Allah the Exalted, and described themselves as having power over what they did not describe Allah as having power over, just as the Magians affirmed for Satan from power over evil what they did not affirm for Allah the Exalted. So they were the Magians of this community, since they followed the religion of the Magians, clung to their sayings, inclined to their falsehoods, caused people to despair of the mercy of Allah the Exalted, made them despair of His spirit, and judged the sinners to be in the Fire eternally, contrary to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And He forgives what is beneath that for whom He wills' (Q 4:48). And they claimed that whoever enters the Fire will not emerge from it, contrary to what has come in the transmission from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that Allah the Exalted will bring out a people from the Fire after they have been burnt in it and become cinders. And they rejected that Allah has a face, despite His saying: 'And the face of your Lord will remain, full of majesty and honor' (Q 55:27). And they denied that Allah has hands, despite His saying: 'When I created with My hands' (Q 38:75). And they denied that He has an eye, despite His saying: 'Sailing under Our eyes' (Q 54:14), and His saying: 'And so that you may be made under My eye' (Q 20:39). And they denied what was transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from his saying: 'Indeed Allah descends to the lowest heaven'—and I shall mention that, Allah willing, chapter by chapter—and with Him is assistance and support, and from Him is success and guidance.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and enumeration of the errors of the Qadariyya/Mu'tazila. Ibn Asakir begins by describing their motivations: they followed their leaders and predecessors in interpreting the Qur'an by their own opinions without divine authority or proof, thereby contradicting the transmissions of the Companions. The first specific error listed is their denial of the believers' vision of Allah in the Hereafter, despite numerous successive reports from the Prophet. He then mentions their denial of the Prophet's intercession, their rejection of the punishment of the grave, and their affirmation that the Qur'an is created—likening this to the polytheists who called the Qur'an 'human speech.' Next, he highlights their belief that humans create their own evil deeds, which he compares to the Magian dualism of two creators: one for good, one for evil. This leads to a series of points: they claimed that Allah wills what does not happen and that what He does not wills happens, in opposition to the consensus of Muslims that Allah's will is effective. He cites multiple Qur'anic verses to refute this, including 'You do not will unless Allah wills.' He then notes that the Prophet called them the 'Magians of this community' because they adopted the Magian belief in two creators. The passage further accuses them of claiming independent power over their own benefit and harm, as well as self-sufficiency from Allah. They are said to have denied that Allah has a face, hands, and eyes—attributes affirmed in the Qur'an—and rejected the hadith of Allah's descent to the lowest heaven. Throughout, Ibn Asakir emphasizes that these positions contradict the consensus of Muslims and the transmitted reports from the Prophet.

Key Terms
رؤية الله
شفاعة
عذاب القبر
القدرية
التابعون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Qadariyya only denied predestination and did not reject other core Sunni beliefs.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows they also denied seeing Allah, intercession, and punishment of the grave, contradicting established transmissions and consensus.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, which three beliefs did the Qadariyya deny?
A) Seeing Allah, intercession, punishment of the grave
B) Unity of Allah, prophethood, resurrection
C) Angels, scriptures, messengers
D) Creation of the world, divine knowledge, power

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya contradicted the Companions by denying clear doctrines like seeing Allah, intercession, and punishment of the grave, despite abundant transmitted evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a religious teaching that your mind finds difficult, do you default to rational interpretation like the Qadariyya, or do you submit to what the Companions transmitted? What will you do the next time a doctrine like 'punishment of the grave' feels uncomfortable?
?
The Qadariyya imitated their leaders. Who are you following in your religious views—scholars whom you've blindly accepted, or have you personally verified their positions against the consensus of the early Muslims?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow and He asked you why you denied intercession or grave punishment, would your answer be based on transmitted evidence or your own reasoning? What change must you make today to align your beliefs with those of the Companions?

Refuting Creation of Qur'an and Human Creation of Evil
Ibn Asakir refutes creation of Qur'an and human creation of evil, linking to Magian dualism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir refutes the Qadariyya's beliefs in the creation of the Qur'an and that humans create evil, comparing them to Magian dualism.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya made humans creators of evil and denied Allah's effective will, echoing the Magians.

Ibn Asakir continues his refutation by targeting two more Qadariyya errors: their claim that the Qur'an is created (like human speech) and that humans create their own evil deeds. He immediately draws a parallel to the Magians, who believed in two creators—one for good and one for evil. He also shows how they denied Allah's effective will (mashi'a), asserting that what Allah does not will can happen, which contradicts clear Qur'anic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation to identify the two main errors: creation of Qur'an and human creation of evil.
Notice the phrase 'نظيرا لقول إخوانهم من المشركين' and 'نظيرا لقول المجوس'.
2
Understand the Magian comparison
Ibn Asakir equates the Qadariyya's belief that humans create evil with the Magian belief in two creators. Find where he says they are the 'Magians of this community'.
This is a strong polemical move, associating them with a non-Islamic dualist religion.
3
Examine the denial of Allah's will
The Qadariyya claimed that Allah wills what does not happen and that what He does not will happens. Ibn Asakir quotes several Qur'anic verses to refute this, such as 'You do not will unless Allah wills'.
This shows that the Qadariyya's view of human agency leads to a flawed understanding of divine will.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why Ibn Asakir groups these errors together: they all undermine Allah's sovereignty and the authority of revelation.

Source Text

ذلك أن الله وأهل القدر مالت بهم أهواؤهم إلى التقليد لرؤسائهم ومن مضى من أسلافهم فتأولوا القرآن على آرائهم تأويلا لم ينزل الله به سلطانا ولا أوضح به برهانا، ولا نقلوه عن رسول رب العالمين ولا عن السلف المتقدمين فخالفوا رواية الصحابة عن نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رؤية الله بالأبصار، وقد جاءت في ذلك الروايات من الجهات المختلفات وتواترت بها الآثار وتتابعت بها الأخبار وأنكروا شفاعة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وردوا الرواية عن السلف المتقدمين وجحدوا عذاب القبر وأن الكفار في قبورهم يعذبون وقد أجمع على ذلك الصحابة والتابعون ودانوا بخلق القرآن نظيرا لقول إخوانهم من المشركين الذين قالوا إن هذا إلا قول البشر، فزعموا أن القرآن كقول البشر وأثبتوا وأيقنوا أن العباد يخلقون الشر نظيرا لقول المجوس الذين يثبتون خالقين أحدهما يخلق الخير والآخر يخلق الشر، وزعمت القدرية أن الله تعالى يخلق الخير وأن الشيطان يخلق الشر وزعموا أن الله عز وجل يشاء ما لا يكون ويكون ما لا يشاء خلافا لما أجمع عليه المسلمون من أن ما شاء الله كان وما لا يشاء لا يكون وردا لقول الله (وما تشاءون إلا أن يشاء الله) فاخبر أنا لا نشاء شيئا إلا وقد شاء أن نشاءه أو لقوله (ولو شاء الله ما اقتتلوا) ولقوله (ولو شئنا لآتينا كل نفس هداها) ولقوله تعالى (فعال لما يريد) ولقوله مخبرا عن شعيب إنه قال (وما يكون لنا أن نعود فيها إلا أن يشاء الله ربنا) ولهذا سماهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مجوس هذه الأمة لأنهم دانوا بديانة المجوس وضاهوا أقوالهم وزعموا أن للخير والشر خالقين كما زعمت المجوس وأنه يكون من الشر ما لا يشاء الله كما قالت المجوس ذلك وزعموا أنهم يملكون الضر والنفع لأنفسهم ردا لقول الله تعالى (قل لا أملك لنفسي ضرا ولا نفعا إلا ما شاء الله) وانحرافا عن القرآن وعما أجمع المسلمون عليه وزعموا أنهم ينفردون بالقدرة على أعمالهم دون ربهم وأثبتوا لأنفسهم غنى عن الله عز وجل، ووصفوا أنفسهم بالقدرة على ما لم يصفوا الله بالقدرة عليه، كما أثبت المجوس للشيطان من القدرة على الشر ما لم يثبتوه الله عز وجل فكانوا مجوس هذه الأمة إذ دانوا بديانة المجوس وتمسكوا بأقوالهم ومالوا إلى أضاليلهم وقنطوا الناس من رحمة الله تعالى وأيسوهم من روحه وحكموا على العصاة بالنار والخلود خلافا لقول الله تعالى (ويغفر ما دون ذلك لمن يشاء) وزعموا أن من دخل النار لا يخرج منها خلافا لما جاءت به الرواية عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن الله عز وجل يخرج من النار قوما بعد ما امتحشوا فيها وصاروا حمما ودفعوا أن يكون لله وجه مع قوله (ويبقى وجه ربك ذو الجلال والإكرام) وأنكروا أن يكون لله يدان مع قوله (لما خلقت بيدي) وأنكروا أن يكون له عين مع قوله (تجري بأعيننا) ولقوله (ولتصنع على عيني) ونفوا ما روي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من قوله (إن الله ينزل إلى السماء الدنيا) وأنا ذاكر ذلك إن شاء الله بابا بابا وبه المعونة والتأييد ومنه التوفيق والتسديد
That is because the people of Qadr (Qadariyya) were led by their desires to imitate their leaders and those who passed from their predecessors, so they interpreted the Qur'an according to their opinions, an interpretation for which Allah sent down no authority and made clear no proof, and they did not transmit it from the Messenger of the Lord of the Worlds nor from the earlier predecessors. So they contradicted the transmission of the Companions from the Prophet of Allah (peace be upon him) concerning seeing Allah with the eyes, and the reports have come about that from various directions, and the narrations have been transmitted successively, and the traditions have followed one after another. And they denied the intercession of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), rejected the transmission from the earlier predecessors, denied the punishment of the grave and that the disbelievers are punished in their graves, though the Companions and the Successors have agreed upon that. And they professed the creation of the Qur'an, analogous to the saying of their brothers from the polytheists who said, 'This is nothing but the words of a human being.' So they claimed that the Qur'an is like human speech. And they affirmed and believed that the servants create evil, analogous to the saying of the Magians who affirm two creators, one creating good and the other creating evil. And the Qadariyya claimed that Allah the Exalted creates good and that Satan creates evil, and they claimed that Allah the Exalted wills what does not happen and what He does not will happens, contrary to what the Muslims have agreed upon—that whatever Allah wills happens, and what He does not will does not happen—and in rejection of the saying of Allah: 'And you do not will unless Allah wills' (Q 76:30), for He informed that we do not will anything unless He has willed that we will it; or of His saying: 'And if Allah had willed, they would not have fought' (Q 2:253); and His saying: 'And if We had willed, We could have guided every soul' (Q 32:13); and His saying the Exalted: 'Doer of whatever He wills' (Q 85:16); and His saying, informing about Shu'ayb: 'And it is not for us to return to it unless Allah, our Lord, wills' (Q 7:89). For this reason, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) called them the Magians of this community, because they followed the religion of the Magians and resembled their sayings. And they claimed that there are two creators for good and evil, just as the Magians claimed, and that there occurs from evil what Allah does not will, as the Magians said that. And they claimed that they possess harm and benefit for themselves, in rejection of the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Say: I do not possess for myself harm or benefit except what Allah wills' (Q 7:188), and in deviation from the Qur'an and from what the Muslims have agreed upon. And they claimed that they are independent in power over their actions without their Lord, and they affirmed for themselves independence from Allah the Exalted, and described themselves as having power over what they did not describe Allah as having power over, just as the Magians affirmed for Satan from power over evil what they did not affirm for Allah the Exalted. So they were the Magians of this community, since they followed the religion of the Magians, clung to their sayings, inclined to their falsehoods, caused people to despair of the mercy of Allah the Exalted, made them despair of His spirit, and judged the sinners to be in the Fire eternally, contrary to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And He forgives what is beneath that for whom He wills' (Q 4:48). And they claimed that whoever enters the Fire will not emerge from it, contrary to what has come in the transmission from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that Allah the Exalted will bring out a people from the Fire after they have been burnt in it and become cinders. And they rejected that Allah has a face, despite His saying: 'And the face of your Lord will remain, full of majesty and honor' (Q 55:27). And they denied that Allah has hands, despite His saying: 'When I created with My hands' (Q 38:75). And they denied that He has an eye, despite His saying: 'Sailing under Our eyes' (Q 54:14), and His saying: 'And so that you may be made under My eye' (Q 20:39). And they denied what was transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from his saying: 'Indeed Allah descends to the lowest heaven'—and I shall mention that, Allah willing, chapter by chapter—and with Him is assistance and support, and from Him is success and guidance.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and enumeration of the errors of the Qadariyya/Mu'tazila. Ibn Asakir begins by describing their motivations: they followed their leaders and predecessors in interpreting the Qur'an by their own opinions without divine authority or proof, thereby contradicting the transmissions of the Companions. The first specific error listed is their denial of the believers' vision of Allah in the Hereafter, despite numerous successive reports from the Prophet. He then mentions their denial of the Prophet's intercession, their rejection of the punishment of the grave, and their affirmation that the Qur'an is created—likening this to the polytheists who called the Qur'an 'human speech.' Next, he highlights their belief that humans create their own evil deeds, which he compares to the Magian dualism of two creators: one for good, one for evil. This leads to a series of points: they claimed that Allah wills what does not happen and that what He does not wills happens, in opposition to the consensus of Muslims that Allah's will is effective. He cites multiple Qur'anic verses to refute this, including 'You do not will unless Allah wills.' He then notes that the Prophet called them the 'Magians of this community' because they adopted the Magian belief in two creators. The passage further accuses them of claiming independent power over their own benefit and harm, as well as self-sufficiency from Allah. They are said to have denied that Allah has a face, hands, and eyes—attributes affirmed in the Qur'an—and rejected the hadith of Allah's descent to the lowest heaven. Throughout, Ibn Asakir emphasizes that these positions contradict the consensus of Muslims and the transmitted reports from the Prophet.

Key Terms
خلق القرآن
القدرية
المجوس
المشيئة
الخير والشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Qadariyya only held a minority view on free will without associating with dualism.
Correction: Ibn Asakir demonstrates that they explicitly adopted Magian dualism by claiming humans create evil and two creators exist for good and evil.

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet call the Qadariyya the 'Magians of this community' according to Ibn Asakir?
A) Because they worshipped fire
B) Because they believed humans create evil and two creators exist for good and evil
C) Because they denied the Hereafter
D) Because they rejected the Prophethood

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya's belief in human creation of evil and denial of Allah's effective will aligns them with Magian dualism, contradicting the Qur'an and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever blamed Satan or your own bad choices for evil in your life, while forgetting that nothing occurs except by Allah's will? How does this passage call you to submit to His absolute sovereignty, even over what you call 'evil'? What one habit can you change to remind yourself that everything—good and apparent evil—comes from Allah?
?
The Qadariyya thought they were defending God's justice by denying His will extends to evil. Are there areas in your life where you try to 'protect' Allah's reputation by denying His control over difficult events? How does accepting that Allah wills all things—including trials—free you from despair? Name one trial you can now thank Him for, trusting His wisdom.
?
If you believe the Qur'an is Allah's uncreated speech, do you treat it as such in your daily life? Do you approach it with the reverence it deserves, or as if it were human words? This passage warns against reducing the Qur'an to mere creation. What specific change can you make today to honor the Qur'an as Allah's eternal word?

Refuting Denial of Attributes and Eternal Punishment
Ibn Asakir refutes Qadariyya claims of human independence, eternal punishment, and denial of attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir refutes the Qadariyya's claims of human independence from Allah, their denial of Allah's attributes (face, hands, eyes), the hadith of descent, and their belief in eternal punishment for sinners.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's attributes and mercy leads to despair and contradicts the Qur'an and Sunna.

In the final part of this refutation, Ibn Asakir turns to the Qadariyya's claim that humans possess independent power over their benefit and harm, which contradicts the Qur'anic verse 'Say: I do not possess for myself harm or benefit except what Allah wills.' He then attacks their denial of the eternal punishment of sinful believers—they judged that all sinners will remain in the Fire forever, ignoring the verse that Allah forgives whom He wills. Finally, he lists their denial of Allah's attributes (face, hands, eyes) and the hadith of Allah's descent to the lowest heaven.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation to see the range of Qadariyya errors covered: independence from Allah, eternal punishment, denial of attributes, and denial of descent.
Notice the shift from theological errors to scriptural and attribute denials.
2
Identify the claim of independence
Ibn Asakir says they claimed to possess harm and benefit for themselves and to be independent of Allah. Find the Qur'anic verse he cites in refutation.
This refutes their belief in absolute human agency.
3
Examine the issue of eternal punishment
The Qadariyya claimed that sinners will remain in the Fire eternally. Ibn Asakir counters with the verse 'He forgives what is beneath that for whom He wills' and the hadith about removal of people from the Fire.
This shows they denied intercession and mercy.
4
Understand the denial of attributes
They rejected Allah's face, hands, eyes, and the hadith of descent. Ibn Asakir cites specific Qur'anic verses for each to prove them.
This is a classic Ash'ari defense of divine attributes.

ذلك أن الله وأهل القدر مالت بهم أهواؤهم إلى التقليد لرؤسائهم ومن مضى من أسلافهم فتأولوا القرآن على آرائهم تأويلا لم ينزل الله به سلطانا ولا أوضح به برهانا، ولا نقلوه عن رسول رب العالمين ولا عن السلف المتقدمين فخالفوا رواية الصحابة عن نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رؤية الله بالأبصار، وقد جاءت في ذلك الروايات من الجهات المختلفات وتواترت بها الآثار وتتابعت بها الأخبار وأنكروا شفاعة رسول الله صلى And they claimed that they are independent in power over their actions without their Lord, and they affirmed for themselves independence from Allah the Exalted, and described themselves as having power over what they did not describe Allah as having power over, just as the Magians affirmed for Satan from power over evil what they did not affirm for Allah the Exalted. Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what did the Qadariyya claim about the punishment of sinners?
A) Sinners will be punished but eventually forgiven
B) Sinners will remain in the Fire eternally without exit
C) Only disbelievers will be punished
D) There is no punishment after death

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever act as if you possess independent power over your own success or failure, forgetting that every harm and benefit comes only by Allah's will? What would change in your daily life if you truly internalized this?
?
When you see a sinner who persists in evil, do you secretly despair of Allah's mercy for them, or do you hold to the hope that Allah forgives whom He wills? How does the Qadariyya's harsh judgment reflect a lack of trust in Allah's attribute of mercy?
?
Are there any attributes of Allah—like His face, hands, or descent—that you find difficult to accept because they do not fit your human understanding? Will you submit to what the Qur'an and Sunna affirm, or will you fall into the error of denial like the Qadariyya?

The Sunni Creed: Rooted in Revelation, Not Speculation
Ibn Asakir refutes heretical sects and states the source of Sunni creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Sunni creed is based on adherence to the Quran, Sunnah, and the path of the early generations, exemplified by Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and why deviation from this leads to error.

Core Idea
Sunni creed is transmitted tradition, not rational speculation.

Imam Ibn Asakir presents a powerful refutation of various heretical sects, listing their specific denials of divine attributes and intercession. Then, in response to a hypothetical question, he lays out the foundation of the Sunni creed: unswerving adherence to the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the legacy of the Salaf, particularly the path of Ahmad ibn Hanbal. This lesson unpacks that foundational statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with two parts in mind
First, notice Ibn Asakir lists errors of the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, etc. Then note how he shifts to a question-and-answer format to state the Sunni position.
The passage begins with specific denials (face, hands, eyes, descent).
2
Identify the specific heresies mentioned
List the groups named (Mu'tazila, Qadariyya, etc.) and the beliefs they denied (e.g., that sinners may be forgiven, that Allah has a face, etc.).
These are foundational points of Ahl al-Sunna.
3
Analyze the Sunni response: what is its basis?
The answer given is 'adherence to the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Prophet and what was narrated from the Companions... and we are speakers according to what Ahmad ibn Hanbal was upon.' This shows the sources of Sunni theology.
Notice the emphasis on transmitted knowledge over reason.
4
Reflect on the role of Ahmad ibn Hanbal
Why is Ahmad ibn Hanbal singled out? The text praises him as the one who manifested truth amidst misguidance. Understand his significance in preserving Sunni orthodoxy.
He is a key figure in the defense of traditional creed.
5
Connect to broader lesson: authority in kalam
This passage teaches that true Sunni creed is not derived from rational argument alone but from divine revelation and the consensus of the early community. Think about how this contrasts with the method of the sects refuted.
This is a methodological statement.

Source Text

The sinners [will be in] the Fire and eternal duration, contrary to the saying of Allah the Exalted (And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills). And they claimed that whoever enters the Fire will not come out of it, contrary to what has come in the narration from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, will bring out people from the Fire after they have been scorched in it and become embers. And they denied that Allah has a face with His saying (And the Face of your Lord, full of Majesty and Honor, will remain). And they denied that Allah has hands with His saying (When I created with My hands). And they denied that He has an eye with His saying (Under Our eyes) and His saying (That you may be formed under My eye). And they rejected what was narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, of his saying (Indeed, Allah descends to the lowest heaven). And I will mention that, Allah willing, chapter by chapter. And with Him is assistance and support, and from Him is success and guidance. Then if a questioner says: 'You have rejected the saying of the Mu'tazila, Qadariyya, Jahmiyya, Haruriyya, Rafida, and Murji'a; so inform us of your saying which you hold and your religion by which you practice.' It is said to him: 'Our saying which we hold and our religion by which we practice is adherence to the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Prophet, peace be upon him, and what has been narrated from the Companions, the Successors, and the imams of hadith. And we are holding fast to that, and we are speakers according to what Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah brighten his face, elevate his rank, and increase his reward, was upon. And we turn away from whoever contradicts his statement, because he is the virtuous imam, the perfect leader, by whom Allah manifested the truth at the appearance of misguidance, and clarified the path, and suppressed the innovations of the innovators, the deviations of the deviators, and the doubts of the doubters. So the mercy of Allah be upon him, a foremost imam, a great explainer, and upon all the imams of the Muslims.'
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a refutation followed by a statement of creed. It begins by citing specific errors of heretical groups: their denial of intercession for sinners (Mu'tazila), denial of God's face, hands, eyes, and descent (Jahmiyya, etc.). Then a rhetorical question is posed: since you reject these sects, what is your own position? The response is twofold: first, the general principle—adherence to Quran, Sunnah, and the legacy of the Companions, Successors, and hadith scholars; second, specific allegiance to the path of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, who is praised as the defender of truth against innovation. The passage thus establishes that Sunni creed is not based on rational speculation alone but on transmitted authority, with Ahmad ibn Hanbal as a pivotal figure.

التمسك بكتاب الله وسنة نبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Sunni creed is derived primarily from rational argument or philosophy.
Correction: This passage shows that the Sunni creed is explicitly based on divine revelation (Quran and Sunnah) and the transmitted legacy of the early generations, not on speculative reason.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the Sunni creed according to Ibn Asakir's response?
A) Rational argument and philosophical proof
B) Adherence to the Book of Allah, the Sunnah, and the path of Ahmad ibn Hanbal
C) The consensus of the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya
D) The opinions of the early philosophers

Key Takeaway
The Sunni creed is firmly rooted in the Quran, Sunnah, and the legacy of the Salaf, particularly as exemplified by Ahmad ibn Hanbal, not in rational speculation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Asakir declares his creed not by listing beliefs but by stating his source of authority. Do you have a clear, written or mental statement of what your creed is based on—or do you just assume you are Sunni because you disagree with others? Write it down now in one sentence, drawing from this passage.
?
The heretics denied Allah’s attributes because their minds could not accept them. Is there any aspect of Allah’s nature or action that you struggle to accept fully? What does your hesitation reveal about the authority you grant revelation versus your own reasoning? Ask Allah to grant you submission to His words even when they challenge your intellect.
?
Ibn Asakir explicitly names Ahmad ibn Hanbal as his model. Who is the scholar or teacher that most shapes your creed? Are you willing to publicly say, like Ibn Asakir, 'we are speakers according to what he was upon'—even if it means separating from those who disagree? Sit quietly for two minutes and consider the cost of such allegiance.

Prayer Behind Any Imam and Wiping Over Socks
Ibn Asakir affirms prayer behind any imam and wiping over socks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the validity of prayer behind any imam, including a wicked one, and the practice of wiping over leather socks.

Core Idea
Prayer behind a sinful imam is valid; wiping over socks is affirmed.

One of the distinctive Sunni beliefs is that congregational prayers remain valid behind any imam, whether righteous or sinful. This principle is rooted in the practice of the Companions. Alongside this, the lesson affirms the practice of wiping over leather socks as part of the Sunnah, against those who reject it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the two main topics: prayer behind any imam and the ruling on wiping over socks.
2
Understand the ruling on prayer behind a wicked imam
The text states we pray Friday and Eid prayers behind every righteous and wicked imam. Reflect on the implication: the sinfulness of the imam does not invalidate the prayer.
This was demonstrated by Abdullah ibn Umar praying behind al-Hajjaj, a notorious tyrant.
3
Examine the evidence from Ibn Umar
The passage cites Abdullah ibn Umar as a precedent. Consider why his action is authoritative in Sunni creed.
Ibn Umar was known for his adherence to the Sunnah, so his practice sets a clear example.
4
Note the affirmation of wiping over socks
The text affirms wiping over leather socks during residence and travel. This is a distinctive Sunni practice against those who deny it.
This is a practical issue of fiqh that reflects the broader methodology of following the Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ديننا أن نصلى الجمعة والأعياد خلف كل بر وفاجر وكذلك شروط الصلوات الجماعات كما روى عن عبد الله بن عمر أنه كان يصلى خلف الحجاج، وإن المسح على الخفين في الحضر والسفر خلافاً لمن أنكر ذلك ونرى الدعاء لأئمة المسلمين بالصلاح والإقرار بإمامتهم وتضليل من رأى الخروج عليهم إذا ظهر منهم ترك الاستقامة، وندين بترك الخروج عليهم بالسيف وترك القتال في الفتنة
And from our religion is that we pray Friday and the two Eid prayers behind every righteous and wicked (imam), and likewise the conditions of congregational prayers, as was narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar that he used to pray behind al-Hajjaj. And we affirm the wiping over the leather socks in residence and travel, contrary to those who deny that. And we hold the view of supplicating for the welfare of the imams of the Muslims and acknowledging their imamate, and declaring misguided those who consider rebelling against them when they appear to abandon uprightness. And we hold by abandoning rebellion against them with the sword and abandoning fighting in civil strife.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage outlines Sunni political theology. It begins by affirming the permissibility and obligation of praying Friday and Eid prayers behind any imam, whether righteous or wicked, citing the practice of Abdullah ibn Umar praying behind the notorious governor al-Hajjaj. Then it mentions the practice of wiping over the leather socks (khuffs) during travel and residence, against those who deny it. It then commands supplicating for the rulers and acknowledging their authority, and declares those who advocate rebellion misguided. Finally, it explicitly prohibits rebellion with weapons and participation in civil strife (fitna).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that prayer behind a sinful imam is invalid or that one should not pray behind them.
Correction: The text affirms the validity and obligation of praying behind any imam, righteous or wicked, based on the precedent of Ibn Umar and Sunni consensus.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the practice of Abdullah ibn Umar regarding prayer?
A) He refused to pray behind a wicked imam.
B) He prayed behind al-Hajjaj, who was a wicked governor.
C) He only prayed behind righteous imams.
D) He never attended Friday prayers.

Key Takeaway
Prayer behind any imam, even a sinful one, is valid and required; wiping over leather socks is affirmed as part of the Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you learned that the imam at your local mosque committed a major sin, would you still attend Friday prayer behind him? What would your heart say? Are you willing to set aside judgment for the sake of unity?
?
Do you ever mock or look down on those who practice wiping over socks because you follow a different fiqh? How does this lesson challenge your pride and call you to respect the Sunnah?
?
Ibn Umar prayed behind a tyrant. Is there any person or group you have avoided praying with because you considered them sinful? Will you now reconsider and seek the same humility?

Obedience to Rulers and Prohibition of Rebellion
Ibn Asakir commands supplication for rulers and prohibits rebellion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni obligation to supplicate for rulers, acknowledge their authority, and avoid rebellion and civil strife.

Core Idea
Supplicate for rulers, do not rebel; avoid fitna.

Sunni political theology emphasizes loyalty to the Muslim community by supporting the rulers, even if they are unjust, and avoiding rebellion. This lesson explains the duty of supplication for imams and the prohibition of armed uprising and participation in civil strife (fitna).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the obligations towards rulers and the prohibition of rebellion.
2
Understand the positive duties
The text mentions making du'a for the welfare of the imams of the Muslims and acknowledging their imamate. Reflect on why supplication is emphasized.
Supplication for rulers is an act of seeking good for the community and obedience to Allah's command to pray for those in authority.
3
Grasp the negative ruling
The text declares misguided those who advocate rebellion when rulers stray from uprightness. It also prohibits armed rebellion and participation in fitna.
This is a key principle: even if rulers are sinful, rebellion is not permitted.
4
Apply the lesson
Consider how this teaching promotes stability and unity in the Muslim community. The ultimate goal is avoiding bloodshed and social chaos.
Fitna (civil strife) is condemned because it leads to division and destruction.
